Section 1:
Senate File 619 - Introduced SENATE FILE 619 BY COMMITTEE ON APPROPRIATIONS (SUCCESSOR TO SF 591) (SUCCESSOR TO SSB 1188) A BILL FOR An Act relating to the natural hazard mitigation financing 1 program, the disaster recovery housing assistance 2 program, the disaster recovery new housing program, 3 post-loss assignment of benefits, the licensing and 4 regulation of adjusters, appraisers, and umpires, and the 5 Iowa economic emergency fund, and providing penalties, 6 making appropriations, and including effective date and 7 applicability provisions. 8 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA: 9 TLSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko S.F. 619 DIVISION I 1 NATURAL HAZARD MITIGATION FINANCING PROGRAM 2 Section 1. NEW SECTION . 16.230 Definitions. 3 1. âDepartmentâ means the department of homeland security 4 and emergency management. 5 2. âFundâ means the natural hazard mitigation revolving loan 6 fund created in section 29D.4. 7 3. âLoan recipientâ means the same as defined in section 8 29D.2. 9 4. âProgramâ means the natural hazard mitigation financing 10 program created in section 29D.3. 11 5. âProjectâ means the same as defined in section 29D.2. 12 Sec. 2. NEW SECTION . 16.231 Funds and accounts ââ program 13 funds and accounts not part of state general fund. 14 1. The department, in consultation with the authority, 15 may establish and maintain funds or accounts determined to 16 be necessary to carry out the purposes of chapter 29D and 17 shall provide for the funding, administration, investment, 18 restrictions, and disposition of the funds and accounts. 19 Any moneys appropriated to the department and the authority 20 for purposes of paying the costs and expenses associated 21 with the administration of the program shall be administered 22 as determined by the department in consultation with the 23 authority. 24 2. The funds or accounts held by the department or the 25 authority, or a trustee acting on behalf of the department or 26 the authority pursuant to a trust agreement related to the 27 program, shall not be considered part of the general fund of 28 the state, are not subject to appropriation for any other 29 purpose by the general assembly, and in determining a general 30 fund balance shall not be included in the general fund of the 31 state, but shall remain in the funds and accounts maintained 32 by the department or the authority, or a trustee pursuant to a 33 trust agreement. Funds and accounts held by the department or 34 the authority, or a trustee acting on behalf of the department 35 -1- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 1/ 106 S.F. 619 or the authority pursuant to a trust agreement related to the 1 program, are separate dedicated funds and accounts under the 2 administration and control of the department in consultation 3 with the authority. 4 Sec. 3. NEW SECTION . 16.233 Security ââ reserve funds ââ 10 pledges ââ nonliability. 11 1. The authority shall not pledge the 28 faith or credit of the state or of a political subdivision of 29 the state to the payment of any bonds or notes. NEW SECTION . 29D.2 Definitions. 4 As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise 5 requires: 6 1. âAuthorityâ means the Iowa finance authority created in 7 section 16.1A. 8 2. âCostâ means all costs or indebtedness incurred by a loan 9 recipient and determined by the department as reasonable and 10 necessary for carrying out all work necessary or incidental to 11 the accomplishment of a project. 12 3. âDepartmentâ means the department of homeland security 13 and emergency management. 14 4. âDirectorâ means the director of the department of 15 homeland security and emergency management. 16 5. âEligible entityâ means a person that is eligible under 17 the STORM Act to receive a loan under the program. 18 6. âFundâ means the natural hazard mitigation revolving loan 19 fund created in section 29D.4. 20 7. âLoan recipientâ means an eligible entity that has 21 received a loan from the fund. 22 8. âMunicipalityâ means a city, county, sanitary district, 23 state agency, or other governmental body or corporation, or any 24 combination of two or more governmental bodies or corporations 25 acting jointly, in connection with a project. 26 9. âPrivate entityâ means a corporation, limited liability 27 company, trust, estate, partnership, association, or any 28 other legal entity or a legal representative, agent, officer, 29 employee, or assignee of such entity. âPrivate entityâ does not 30 include any of the following: 31 a. An individual, municipality, or city utility as that term 32 is defined in section 362.2. 33 b. A public water supply system as defined in section 34 455B.171. 35 -5- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 5/ 106 S.F. 619 c. A qualified entity as defined in section 384.84, 1 subsection 2. 2 10. âProgramâ means the natural hazard mitigation financing 3 program created in section 29D.3. 4 11. a. âProjectâ means an activity or set of activities, 5 in accordance with the limitations set forth in the STORM Act, 6 that mitigate the impact of natural hazards, including but not 7 limited to: 8 (1) Drought and prolonged episodes of intense heat. 9 (2) Severe storms, including tornadoes, windstorms, and 10 severe winter storms. 11 (3) Wildfires. 12 (4) Earthquakes. 13 (5) Flooding. 14 (6) Shoreline erosion. 15 (7) High water levels. 16 (8) Storm surges. 17 b. âProjectâ may include but is not limited to any of the 18 following: 19 (1) The construction, repair, or replacement of a 20 nonfederal levee or other flood control structure, provided 21 that the administrator of the federal emergency management 22 agency, in consultation with the United States army corps of 23 engineers, if appropriate, requires an eligible entity to 24 determine that such levee or other flood control structure is 25 designed, constructed, and maintained in accordance with sound 26 engineering practices and standards equivalent to the purpose 27 for which such levee or structure is intended. 28 (2) Zoning and land use planning changes. 29 (3) Establishing and enforcing building codes. 30 12. âSafeguarding tomorrow through ongoing risk mitigation 31 Actâ , or âSTORM Actâ , means the federal Robert T. Stafford 32 Disaster Relief and Emergency Assistance Act, Pub. L. No. 33 93-288, as amended, 42 U.S.C. Â§5121 et seq. 34 Sec. 7. NEW SECTION . 29D.4 Natural hazard mitigation 17 revolving loan fund. 18 1. The fund shall consist of moneys appropriated by 30 the general assembly, moneys received by the fund through the 31 federal emergency management agency and the STORM Act, moneys 32 received as repayment of loan principal and interest from loans 33 paid for by the fund, and all other moneys received by the fund 34 from any other source. Notwithstanding section 8.33, moneys in 35 -7- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 7/ 106 S.F. 619 the fund that remain unencumbered or unobligated at the close 1 of the fiscal year shall not revert but shall remain available 2 for expenditure for the purposes designated. Notwithstanding 3 section 12C.7, subsection 2, interest or earnings on moneys in 4 the fund shall be credited to the fund. 5 b. Moneys in the fund are appropriated to the department to 6 provide loans to eligible entities pursuant to section 29D.9, 7 and for administration of the program as permitted under the 8 STORM Act. Moneys in the fund shall not be used to provide a 9 loan to a private entity for the acquisition of real property. 10 Moneys in the fund shall not be considered part of the general 11 fund of the state subject to appropriation for any other 12 purpose by the general assembly, and in determining a general 13 fund balance, shall not be included in the general fund of 14 the state subject to section 16.31, insofar as section 16.31 15 complies with the STORM Act. 16 Sec. 9. The public adjuster 14 shall provide notice of the insuredâs rights under chapter 15 555A, and the insured may rescind the contract as provided in 16 chapter 555A. If the insured rescinds the contract, 19 anything of value given by the insured shall be returned to the 20 insured within fifteen business days following receipt of the 21 cancellation notice by the public adjuster. 22 b. A contract provision shall not be redacted in a copy of 23 the contract submitted to the commissioner. Such redaction 24 shall constitute a violation of this chapter, and shall be 25 subject to penalties under sections 522C.13 and 522C.14. 26 2. If the insurer, no later than five calendar days 27 after the date on which the insuredâs loss is reported to 28 the insurer, either pays or commits in writing to pay to the 29 insured the policy limit of the insuredâs insurance policy, the 30 public adjuster shall: 31 a. Only be entitled to reasonable compensation from the 34 insured for services provided on behalf of the insured based on 35 -35- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 35/ 106 S.F. 619 the time spent on the claim, and the expenses incurred by the 1 public adjuster, until the date the insurer pays the claim or 2 provides the insured with a written commitment that the insurer 3 will pay the claim. 4 3. A public adjuster contract shall not contain a provision 5 that does any of the following: 6 a. Allows the public adjusterâs percentage of a settlement 7 to be collected if money is still due from an insurer, or that 8 allows the public adjuster to collect the entire percentage 9 of a settlement from any single payment issued by an insurer 10 rather than as a percentage of each payment issued by the 11 insurer. 12 b. PROPERTY INSURANCE POLICIES OBLIGATE THE INSURED TO 1 PRESENT A CLAIM TO THE INSUREDâS INSURER FOR CONSIDERATION. 2 THERE ARE THREE TYPES OF ADJUSTERS THAT MAY BE INVOLVED IN THAT 3 PROCESS. THE THREE TYPES ARE AS FOLLOWS: 4 (A) âSTAFF ADJUSTERâ IS DEFINED IN IOWA CODE SECTION 522C.2. 5 A STAFF ADJUSTER IS EMPLOYED BY THE INSURER. THEY WILL NOT 6 CHARGE THE INSURED A FEE. 7 (B) âINDEPENDENT ADJUSTERâ IS DEFINED IN IOWA CODE SECTION 8 522C.2. AN INDEPENDENT ADJUSTER IS CONTRACTED BY THE INSURER 9 TO REPRESENT THE INSURER. THEY WILL NOT CHARGE THE INSURED A 10 FEE. 11 (C) âPUBLIC ADJUSTERâ IS DEFINED IN IOWA CODE SECTION 12 522C.2. A PUBLIC ADJUSTER IS NOT AN EMPLOYEE OR REPRESENTATIVE 13 OF THE INSURER. THEY ARE HIRED BY THE INSURED TO ASSIST IN THE 14 PREPARATION, PRESENTATION, AND SETTLEMENT OF A CLAIM. 15 2. THE INSURED IS NOT REQUIRED TO HIRE A PUBLIC ADJUSTER 16 TO HELP THE INSURED MEET THE INSUREDâS OBLIGATIONS UNDER THE 17 INSUREDâS POLICY, BUT HAS THE RIGHT TO DO SO. 18 3. THE INSURED HAS THE RIGHT TO INITIATE DIRECT 19 COMMUNICATIONS WITH THE INSUREDâS ATTORNEY, THE INSUREDâS 20 INSURANCE COMPANY, THE INSURANCE COMPANYâS STAFF ADJUSTER OR 21 INDEPENDENT ADJUSTER, THE INSURANCE COMPANYâS ATTORNEY, OR ANY 22 OTHER PERSON REGARDING THE SETTLEMENT OF THE INSUREDâS CLAIM. 23 4. THE INSURED MAY BE RESPONSIBLE FOR ANY AMOUNT PAYABLE TO 24 A PUBLIC ADJUSTER RELATED TO ANY PORTION OF A CLAIM THAT WAS 25 PREVIOUSLY PAID IN PART, IN FULL, OR SETTLED BY THE INSURER 26 PRIOR TO A CONTRACT BEING ENTERED INTO BETWEEN THE PUBLIC 27 ADJUSTER AND THE INSURED. 28 5. THE AMOUNT PAYABLE TO A PUBLIC ADJUSTER, WHICH CAN 29 INCLUDE A SALARY, FEE, COMMISSION, OR OTHER CONSIDERATION AS 30 OUTLINED IN THE CONTRACT, IS THE OBLIGATION OF THE INSURED, NOT 31 THE INSURER. 32 6. THE INSURED MAY FILE A COMPLAINT WITH THE IOWA INSURANCE 33 DIVISION BY CALLING (877) 955-1212 OR VISITING IID.IOWA.GOV. 34 5. An original copy of a completed contract shall be 35 -37- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 37/ 106 S.F. 619 provided to the public adjuster and to the insured. NEW SECTION . 522C.11 Adjusters ââ standards of 16 conduct. 17 1. A public adjuster shall serve with objectivity and 18 complete loyalty to the interest of the insured. A public 19 adjuster shall render to the insured in good faith information, 20 counsel, and service, that in the opinion of the public 21 adjuster will best serve the insuredâs insurance claim needs 22 and interest. These duties extend to the claims process and 23 include providing timely responses to both the insurer and the 24 insured. 25 2. For a minimum of seventy-two hours following a 26 catastrophic disaster, to allow time for the commissioner 27 to safely deploy consumer protection resources, a public 28 adjuster shall not, in person or by telephone, directly offer 29 to contract, attempt to offer to contract, or enter into an 30 adjuster contract with an insured unless the offer to contract, 31 the attempt to offer to contract, or entering into a contract 32 is initiated by a consumer. If the commissioner deems the 33 severity of the catastrophic disaster to have placed people 34 under duress, the commissioner shall immediately dispatch the 35 -38- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 38/ 106 S.F. 619 consumer advocate and other personnel to the disaster area to 1 provide consumer guidance. If, after a public hearing, the 2 commissioner determines that, due to the scope and severity 3 of the catastrophic disaster, additional time is necessary to 4 safely deploy additional consumer protection resources, the 5 commissioner may extend the time period that a public adjuster 6 shall not offer to contract, attempt to offer to contract, or 7 enter into a contract for an additional seventy-two hours. 8 3. A public adjuster shall not solicit between the hours 9 of 8:00 p.m. and 9:00 a.m. Solicitation shall include but is 10 not limited to a door-to-door sale as that term is defined in 11 section 555A.1. 12 4. A public adjuster, or an independent adjuster, shall not 13 permit an unlicensed employee or representative of the public 14 adjuster or independent adjuster, nor any person associated 15 with a claim, to conduct business for which a license is 16 required under this chapter. 17 5. An adjuster shall not have a direct or indirect financial 18 interest in any aspect of a claim other than the amount payable 19 pursuant to the written contract with an insured under section 20 522C.10. 21 6. An adjuster shall not acquire any interest in salvage of 22 property. 23 7. An adjuster shall not undertake the adjustment of any 24 claim if the adjuster is not competent and knowledgeable as 25 to the terms and conditions of the insurance coverage, or if 26 the loss or coverage otherwise exceeds the adjusterâs current 27 expertise. 28 8. An adjuster shall maintain all documentation relating to 29 all estimates and coverage determinations for a minimum of five 30 years from the date of completion of a settlement. 31 9. An adjuster shall not knowingly make any false oral or 32 written material statements regarding any person engaged in the 33 business of insurance, or any other adjuster, to an insured who 34 is a client or potential client. 35 -39- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 39/ 106 S.F. 619 10. a. An adjuster shall not reasonably act, or fail to 1 act, in any manner that obstructs or prevents an insurer or 2 adjuster from timely conducting an inspection of any part of 3 an insuredâs property for which there is a claim for loss or 4 damage. 5 b. If a public adjuster is unavailable after reasonable 6 request by an insurer, resulting in delay of the insurerâs 7 timely inspection of the property, the insured shall allow 8 the insurer to have access to the property without the 9 participation or presence of the public adjuster to facilitate 10 the insurerâs prompt inspection of the loss or damage. 11 11. An adjuster shall respond to an inquiry from an insurer 12 or an insured regarding a claim within fifteen business days 13 of the date of the inquiry unless good cause exists for delay. 14 The adjuster shall reply within fifteen business days to all 15 pertinent communications from the insured, the insurer, or a 16 representative of the insured or the insurer that reasonably 17 suggest that a response is expected. 18 12. Upon receiving notification of a claim, an insurer shall 19 provide necessary claim forms, instructions, and reasonable 20 assistance within fifteen business days of notification of the 21 claim so that first-party claimants can comply with the policy 22 conditions and the insurerâs reasonable requirements. 23 13. An adjuster shall not act as an appraiser and as an 24 adjuster on the same claim. 25 14. An adjuster shall not act as an umpire and as an 26 adjuster on the same claim. 27 15. A public adjuster shall not enter into a contract that 28 accepts a power of attorney or limited power of attorney for 29 an insured. 30 16. a. An independent adjuster shall not act as an 31 independent adjuster and a public adjuster on the same claim. 32 b. A public adjuster shall not act as a public adjuster and 33 an independent adjuster on the same claim. 34 17. A staff adjuster may be licensed as a public adjuster 35 -40- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 40/ 106 S.F. 619 or as an independent adjuster, but shall be prohibited from 1 providing services as an independent adjuster or a public 2 adjuster while employed as a staff adjuster. 3 18. A public adjuster shall not agree to, or reject, any 4 loss settlement without the insuredâs express knowledge and 5 written consent. 6 19. An adjuster shall not engage in any act or practice 7 that is a conflict of interest. A conflict of interest shall 8 include but is not limited to the following: 9 a. A direct or indirect financial interest with a person 10 responsible for the reconstruction, repair, or restoration of 11 damaged property that is the subject of a claim, or with a 12 person involved in resolving a claim valuation dispute. 13 b. Being an owner, employee, agent, investor, or having 19 other financial interest in a business entity responsible for 20 the reconstruction, repair, or restoration of damaged property 21 that is the subject of a claim, or having an immediate family 22 member who is an owner, employee, agent, or investor in a 23 business entity responsible for the reconstruction, repair, 24 or restoration of a damaged property that is the subject of a 25 claim. 26 d. Entering into a written or verbal contract, or formal 27 or informal agreement, with any person that compromises the 28 adjusterâs duty of loyalty to the insured. 29 e. Using claim information obtained in the course of a claim 30 investigation for commercial purposes including marketing or 31 advertising for the benefit of the adjuster. 32 20. A public adjuster shall not file a complaint with 33 the division on behalf of an insured without the insuredâs 34 knowledge and written consent. 35 -41- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 41/ 106 S.F. 619 21. An adjuster shall not represent, directly or 1 indirectly, that damage has occurred at a property unless the 2 adjuster has inspected the damaged areas of the property. 3 22. An adjuster shall produce a detailed written estimate to 4 repair or replace covered damages and provide a copy to both 5 the insured and the insurer in a timely manner. 6 23. A public adjuster shall not offer to pay an insuredâs 7 deductible, or claim that the insuredâs deductible will be 8 waived, as an inducement to use the services of the public 9 adjuster. 10 24. An adjuster shall respond reasonably promptly to 11 inquiries by the division. 12 25. A public adjuster shall provide a detailed invoice for 13 completed services to an insured prior to requesting payment 14 for services pursuant to a contract under section 522C.10. 15 26. Funds received or held by a public adjuster on behalf of 16 an insured toward the settlement of a claim shall be: 17 a. Held in a fiduciary capacity. 18 b. Deposited by the adjuster into one or more separate 19 noninterest-bearing fiduciary trust accounts in a financial 20 institution licensed to do business in this state no later 21 than the close of the fifth business day from the date the 22 public adjuster received the funds, and either deposited in the 23 insuredâs name or in the name of the public adjuster as trustee 24 for the insured, to be held and administered as a trust account 25 for the benefit and protection of the insured. 26 c. NEW SECTION . 522C.14 Civil and criminal penalties. 31 1. a. Upon receipt of a certificate of noncompliance under 3 subsection 1, the commissioner shall issue a notice to the 4 adjuster that the division will, unless the certificate of 5 noncompliance is withdrawn, deny the adjusterâs application 6 for license issuance, renewal, reinstatement, or reissuance, 7 suspend the adjusterâs current license, or revoke the 8 adjusterâs currently suspended license, thirty calendar days 9 after the date the notice is mailed. Notice shall be sent 10 to the adjusterâs last known address by restricted certified 11 mail, return receipt requested, or in accordance with the 12 divisionâs rules for service. The notice shall contain all of 13 the following: 14 a. A statement that the commissioner intends to deny 15 the adjusterâs application for license issuance, renewal, 16 reinstatement, or reissuance; suspend the adjusterâs current 17 license; or revoke the adjusterâs currently suspended license 18 in thirty calendar days unless the certificate of noncompliance 19 is withdrawn. 20 b. A statement that the adjuster must contact the agency 21 that issued the certificate of noncompliance to request a 22 withdrawal. 23 c. A statement that the adjuster does not have a right to 24 a hearing before the division, but that the adjuster may file 25 an application for a hearing in district court pursuant to 26 section 252J.9 or 272D.9, as applicable, and that the filing 27 of an application by the adjuster will stay the proceedings of 28 the division. 29 d. A copy of the certificate of noncompliance. 30 3. An adjuster shall keep the commissioner informed of all 31 actions taken by the district court or the issuing agency in 32 connection with a certificate of noncompliance. Within seven 33 calendar days of filing or issuance, an adjuster shall provide 34 to the commissioner a copy of all applications filed with the 35 -52- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 52/ 106 S.F. 619 district court pursuant to an application or hearing, all 1 court orders entered in such action, and all withdrawals of a 2 certificate of noncompliance. 3 4. If an applicant or licensed adjuster timely files an 4 application for hearing in district court and the division 5 is notified of the filing, the commissionerâs denial, 6 suspension, or revocation proceedings shall be stayed until 7 the division is notified by the district court, the issuing 8 agency, the licensee, or the applicant of the resolution of 9 the application. Upon receipt of a court order lifting the 10 stay or otherwise directing the commissioner to proceed, the 11 commissioner shall continue with the intended action described 12 in the notice. 13 5. If the commissioner does not receive a withdrawal of 14 the certificate of noncompliance from the issuing agency, or a 15 notice from a clerk of court, the issuing agency, the licensee, 16 or the applicant that an application for hearing has been filed 17 within thirty calendar days after the notice is issued, the 18 commissioner shall deny the adjusterâs application for license 19 issuance, renewal, reinstatement, or reissuance; suspend a 20 current license; or revoke a currently suspended license. 21 6. Upon receipt of a withdrawal of a certificate of 22 noncompliance from the issuing agency, suspension or revocation 23 proceedings shall halt and the named adjuster shall be notified 24 that the proceedings have halted. If the adjusterâs license 25 has already been suspended, the adjuster must apply for 26 reinstatement in accordance with section 522C.15, and the 27 license shall be reinstated if the adjuster is otherwise in 28 compliance with this chapter. If the adjusterâs application 29 for licensure was stayed, application processing shall resume. 30 All fees required for license renewal, reinstatement, or 31 reissuance must be paid by the adjuster, and all continuing 32 education requirements shall be satisfied, before the 33 adjusterâs license is renewed or reinstated after a license 34 suspension or revocation under this chapter. 35 -53- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 53/ 106 S.F. 619 7. NEW SECTION . 522F.1 Definitions. 23 As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise 24 requires: 25 1. âAdjusterâ means a person licensed pursuant to chapter 26 522C. 27 2. âAmount of lossâ means the monetary amount determined 28 to be necessary to properly repair or replace damage related 29 to the scope of a loss for a covered peril, and is limited to 30 all applicable coverages for covered items associated with the 31 claim. 32 3. âAppraiserâ means a person licensed as an appraiser 33 pursuant to section 522F.4. 34 4. âAppraiser listâ means a list, maintained by the 35 -55- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 55/ 106 S.F. 619 division, of all appraisers licensed by the division. 1 5. âClaimantâ means a person who makes a first-party claim 2 under a policy of property and casualty insurance. 3 6. âCommissionerâ means the commissioner of insurance. 4 7. âDisciplinary matterâ means an individual is the subject 5 of an investigation, complaint, pending administrative action, 6 or other such action in any state. 7 8. âFirst-party claimâ means a claim filed by a named 8 insured under an insurance policy against which a claim is 9 made. 10 9. âGood causeâ means a legally sufficient reason including 11 but not limited to any of the following: 12 a. A conflict of interest. 13 b. A lack of independence or an inability to competently or 14 promptly carry out the duties required under this chapter. 15 c. Any other reason that would reasonably be expected to 16 impair an appraisal. 17 10. âImmediate familyâ means an individualâs parent, 18 sibling, child, grandchild, spouse, spouses of the individualâs 19 children, or parents of the individualâs spouse. 20 11. âInsuredâ means a person covered under an insurance 21 policy against which a claim is made. 22 12. âInsurerâ means a person engaged in the business of 23 insurance and regulated under chapter 507A, 508, 512B, 515, 24 518, 518A, or 520. 25 13. âNIPR gatewayâ means the communication network developed 26 and operated by the national insurance producer registry that 27 links state insurance regulators with regulated entities to 28 facilitate the electronic exchange of adjuster information, 29 including but not limited to license applications, license 30 renewals, appointments, and terminations. 31 14. âPartyâ means an insurer or a claimant, including an 32 employee, contractor, and other representative of an insurer 33 or claimant. 34 15. âPersonâ means an individual or a business entity. 35 -56- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 56/ 106 S.F. 619 16. âReinstatementâ means the reinstatement of a suspended 1 license which was suspended in connection with a disciplinary 2 matter, and that has not expired or been terminated during the 3 suspension period. 4 17. âReissuanceâ means the issuance of a new license 5 following the revocation of a license, the suspension and 6 subsequent termination of a license, or the forfeiture of a 7 license in connection with a disciplinary matter. 8 18. âUmpireâ means a person licensed as an umpire pursuant 9 to section 522F.9. 10 19. âUmpire listâ means a list, maintained by the division, 11 of all umpires licensed by the division. 12 Sec. 57. NEW SECTION . 522F.3 Appraiserâs license ââ 16 eligibility. 17 1. A person shall not act as, or represent that the person 18 is, an appraiser in this state unless the person is licensed 19 under this chapter. Have experience or training in building construction, 29 repair, or estimating property damage. 30 b. Unless waived by the commissioner based on the personâs 31 other professional qualifications, have a minimum of three 32 yearsâ experience as any of the following: 33 (1) A professional engineer licensed under chapter 542B or 34 similarly licensed in another state. 35 -57- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 57/ 106 S.F. 619 (2) An architect licensed under chapter 544A or similarly 1 licensed in another state. 2 (3) An adjuster licensed under chapter 522C or similarly 3 licensed in another state. 4 (4) A residential contractor as defined in section 103A.71. 5 (5) A contractor registered under chapter 91C or similarly 6 registered in another state. 7 c. NEW SECTION . 522F.6 Appraisers ââ payment. 1 1. Each party to an appraisal shall be responsible for the 2 following: 3 a. The partyâs own appraiserâs fees and expenses. 4 b. An equal share of all reasonable and necessary fees and 5 expenses incurred by an umpire, if necessary. 6 c. An equal share of all reasonable and necessary costs 7 incurred in the course of conducting the appraisal. 8 2. a. An appraiser shall not charge any party on a basis 9 dependent on the outcome of the written itemized award, or 10 charge in a manner that relies on a barter arrangement, gift, 11 favor, or in-kind exchange. 12 b. Prior to the conclusion of an appraisal process via 13 final settlement or issuance of a written itemized award by 14 an umpire, an appraiser shall not require, demand, or accept 15 any fee, retainer, compensation, deposit, or other type 16 of consideration, unless the loss is being handled by the 17 appraiser on a time-plus-expense basis. 18 3. An appraiser shall not charge, and is not entitled to, 19 a fee, compensation, deposit, or other type of consideration 20 if the appraiser abandons the appraisal prior to the umpire 21 issuing a written itemized award. 22 Sec. 62. NEW SECTION . 522F.7 Appraisers ââ standards of 23 conduct. 24 1. An appraiser shall act with due diligence, including but 25 not limited to demonstrating accuracy, fairness, and timeliness 26 throughout an appraisal process. 27 2. a. (1) No later than five business days after being 28 hired by a party to an appraisal and before beginning work as 29 an appraiser, an appraiser shall disclose to all parties to the 30 appraisal any potential conflict of interest. 31 (2) An appraiser shall not engage in any act or practice 32 that is a conflict of interest during the appraisal. 33 (3) If a conflict of interest arises after the start of the 34 appraisal process, an appraiser shall disclose the conflict of 35 -61- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 61/ 106 S.F. 619 interest to the parties and shall withdraw from the appraisal 1 process no more than five business days after the conflict of 2 interest arose. 3 b. A conflict of interest shall include but is not limited 4 to all of the following: 5 (1) An appraiser is a party to a lawsuit against any party 6 to an appraisal. 7 (2) An appraiser is a party to, or a member or employee 8 of a law firm that represents a party to, a current lawsuit 9 involving an insurer that is a party to the appraisal. 10 (3) An appraiser has personally investigated, prosecuted, 11 or advocated in connection with the appraisal. 12 (4) An appraiser has acted as counsel to any party to 13 an appraisal within the two years immediately preceding the 14 appraisal. 15 (5) An appraiser has a personal financial interest in the 16 outcome of the appraisal or any other significant interest 17 that could be substantially affected by the outcome of the 18 appraisal. 19 (6) A member of an appraiserâs immediate family is any of 20 the following: 21 (a) A party to the appraisal, or an officer, director, or 22 trustee of a party. 23 (b) A current employee of an appraiser or an adjuster to the 24 appraisal. 25 (c) A business entity licensed as an adjuster that adjusted 26 the loss at issue in the appraisal. 27 (d) Known to have an interest that could be substantially 28 affected by the outcome of the appraisal. 29 (e) An immediate family member that has a legally sufficient 30 reason that requires the appraiser to withdraw from the 31 appraisal. 32 3. An appraiser shall postpone an appraisal for a reasonable 33 amount of time if any party demonstrates reasonable cause for 34 a postponement. The appraiser shall notify all parties if 35 -62- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 62/ 106 S.F. 619 the appraisal process is postponed. An appraiserâs failure 1 to timely notify all parties may result in a penalty under 2 sections 522F.20 and 522F.21. 3 4. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall 4 consider all information provided by the parties and any 5 other reasonably available evidence that is material to the 6 appraisal. 7 5. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall 8 carefully decide all issues submitted for determination of the 9 amount of loss and actual cash value. 10 6. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall provide 11 all parties a fair and reasonable itemized written appraisal 12 detailing the amount of loss and actual cash value. 13 7. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall ensure 14 the appraiserâs party is reasonably informed of all updates 15 throughout the appraisal process. 16 8. An appraiser shall not permit outside influence to affect 17 an appraisal. 18 9. An appraiser shall not allow a person other than the 19 umpire for the appraisal to determine differences between the 20 actual cash value and the amount of loss of each item on the 21 appraisal. 22 10. a. An appraiser shall not communicate directly or 23 indirectly with any of the following: 24 (1) An opposing party or representative of the opposing 25 party other than the opposing partyâs appraiser. 26 (2) The umpire, unless reasonable notice and opportunity 27 to participate in the communication is provided to an opposing 28 appraiser. 29 b. Notwithstanding paragraph âaâ , an appraiser may 30 communicate with an opposing party or an umpire in order to do 31 any of the following: 32 (1) Identify the partyâs counsel or experts. 33 (2) Discuss logistical matters, including the time and 34 place of a meeting or to make arrangements for the conduct 35 -63- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 63/ 106 S.F. 619 of the appraisal. The appraiser initiating contact with the 1 umpire shall promptly inform an opposing appraiser. 2 (3) If an opposing appraiser fails to participate in a 3 meeting or conference call after receiving reasonable notice 4 and opportunity to participate, or if all parties agree 5 in writing in advance of a meeting or conference call, an 6 appraiser may discuss a claim with the umpire. 7 11. An appraiser shall not act as, or have ever acted as, an 8 adjuster or umpire on the same claim. 9 12. An appraiser shall not withdraw or abandon an appraisal 10 unless compelled by unforeseen circumstances that would render 11 it impossible or impracticable for the appraiser to continue. 12 13. During the appraisal process, an appraiser may hire 13 an outside expert to provide subject matter expertise as 14 necessary. 15 Sec. 63. NEW SECTION . 522F.8 Umpire license ââ eligibility. 16 1. NEW SECTION . 522F.13 Umpires ââ standards of 16 conduct. 17 1. An umpire shall act with due diligence, including but 18 not limited to demonstrating accuracy, fairness, and timeliness 19 throughout an appraisal process. 20 2. a. (1) No later than three business days after being 21 hired by the parties to an appraisal and before beginning work 22 as an umpire to the appraisal, an umpire shall disclose to all 23 parties to the appraisal any potential conflict of interest. 24 If a conflict of interest exists, the umpire shall withdraw 25 from the appraisal. 26 (2) An umpire shall not engage in any act or practice that 27 is a conflict of interest during the appraisal. 28 (3) If a conflict of interest arises after the start of an 29 appraisal process, an umpire shall disclose the conflict of 30 interest to the parties and shall withdraw from the appraisal 31 process. 32 b. A conflict of interest shall include but is not limited 33 to the following: 34 (1) An umpire is a party to a lawsuit against any party to 35 -68- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 68/ 106 S.F. 619 an appraisal. 1 (2) An umpire is a party to, or a member or employee of 2 a law firm that represents a party to, a current lawsuit 3 involving an insurer that is party to the appraisal. 4 (3) An umpire has a personal open claim involving an insurer 5 that is a party to the appraisal. 6 (4) An umpire has a personal bias or prejudice against a 7 party. 8 (5) An umpire has personally investigated, prosecuted, or 9 advocated in connection with the appraisal. 10 (6) An umpire has acted as counsel to any party to an 11 appraisal within the two years immediately preceding the 12 appraisal. 13 (7) An umpire has a personal financial interest in the 14 outcome of the appraisal or any other significant interest 15 that could be substantially affected by the outcome of the 16 appraisal. 17 (8) A member of an umpireâs immediate family is any of the 18 following: 19 (a) A party to the appraisal, or an officer, director, or 20 trustee of a party. 21 (b) A current employee of an appraiser or an adjuster to the 22 appraisal. 23 (c) A business entity licensed as an adjuster that adjusted 24 the loss at issue in the appraisal. 25 (d) Known to have an interest that could be substantially 26 affected by the outcome of the appraisal. 27 (e) An immediate family member that has a legally sufficient 28 reason that requires the umpire to withdraw from the appraisal. 29 3. Prior to beginning work as an umpire, an umpire shall 30 enter into a written contract with all parties to the appraisal 31 that requires the parties and the umpire to comply with this 32 section, and provides that each party shall pay costs as 33 required under section 522F.11. 34 4. An umpire shall not begin work on a claim until the 35 -69- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 69/ 106 S.F. 619 umpire receives each appraiserâs differences in actual cash 1 value and amount of loss of each item of the claim, and written 2 approval from the parties for the umpire to begin work. 3 5. No later than three business days after receiving notice 4 of selection for an appraisal, an umpire shall send notice 5 to the parties and the appraisers that includes all of the 6 following: 7 a. A statement informing each party if the umpire is insured 8 by an insurer. 9 b. A statement informing each party of the partyâs 10 respective right to object to the umpire under section 522F.12. 11 6. An umpire shall address only issues in an appraisal that 12 the appraisers disagree on. 13 7. An umpire shall review all information submitted by the 14 appraisers and parties related to the dispute, including but 15 not limited to the itemized appraisals or estimates, supporting 16 documents, photographs, and diagrams. The umpire shall review 17 the differences between what each appraiser submitted and seek 18 agreement by the appraisers regarding the disputed issues. 19 8. An umpire shall allow each appraiser to a claim a fair 20 opportunity to present evidence and arguments regarding the 21 appraisal. 22 9. An umpire shall ask questions, or request documents or 23 other evidence, as the umpire deems necessary in the course of 24 an appraisal. 25 10. An umpire may accept either appraiserâs scope, 26 quantity, value, or cost regarding an item in dispute, or 27 develop an independent decision on each item in dispute. 28 11. An umpire shall decide all matters in an appraisal 29 fairly, and shall exercise independent judgment and integrity. 30 12. An umpire shall prepare and distribute a written 31 itemized award pursuant to section 522F.16. 32 13. An umpire shall not visit the claimantâs damaged 33 property without consent from all appraisers. 34 14. An umpire shall not withdraw or abandon an appraisal 35 -70- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 70/ 106 S.F. 619 unless compelled by unforeseen circumstances that would render 1 it impossible or impracticable for the umpire to continue on a 2 claim. 3 15. An umpire shall not attend or participate in settlement 4 discussions unless requested to do so by all parties. 5 16. An umpire shall not permit outside influences to affect 6 an appraisal. 7 17. An umpire shall not delegate the umpireâs duty to decide 8 a claim to any other person. 9 18. Unless reasonable notice and opportunity to participate 10 in a communication is provided to an opposing party and the 11 opposing partyâs appraiser, an umpire shall not communicate, 12 directly or indirectly, with any party or appraiser regarding a 13 pending appraisal. 14 19. Unless reasonable notice and opportunity to participate 15 in a communication is provided to all parties, an umpire shall 16 not communicate, directly or indirectly, with any party, a 17 representative of any party, or any other person with a direct 18 or indirect interest in the claim, regarding an issue of fact 19 or law in the appraisal. 20 20. An umpire shall not act as, or have ever acted as, an 21 adjuster or appraiser on the same claim. 22 Sec. 69. NEW SECTION . 522F.14 Appraisal process. 23 1. This section provides for the appraisal process if all 24 of the following apply: 25 a. The claimantâs insurance policy is delivered, issued for 26 delivery, or renewed in this state. 27 b. The property that is the subject of the claimantâs 28 claim is located in this state, or the dispute is subject to 29 jurisdiction in this state. 30 c. A claimant gave proper notice to the claimantâs insurer 31 of a loss claim, and the claimant and insurer dispute the 32 actual cash value of the scope of loss, or the amount of loss 33 the insurer will pay, for the claimantâs claim under the 34 claimantâs policy. The claimant and the insurer must both 35 -71- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 71/ 106 S.F. 619 provide the other party with a scope of loss of a covered 1 peril, including a list stating separately the actual cash 2 value and the amount of claimed loss for each item. 3 d. The claimant or insurer demands in writing an appraisal. 4 2. Within twenty calendar days following either the 5 claimantâs or insurerâs receipt of the other partyâs written 6 demand for an appraisal, the claimant and the insurer 7 shall each select an appraiser from the appraiser list. 8 Upon selection, the appraiser shall attest in writing to 9 the selecting party that the appraiser is competent and 10 disinterested with regards to the appraisal in question. 11 3. a. Within fifteen calendar days of the selection of 12 appraisers pursuant to subsection 2, both appraisers shall 13 agree on an umpire from the umpire list. 14 b. A party or an appraiser may object to the agreed-upon 15 umpire for good cause pursuant to section 522F.12 no later 16 than five business days after the umpire has been selected. A 17 replacement umpire from the umpire list shall then be agreed 18 upon by both appraisers. 19 c. If both appraisers fail to agree on an umpire, either the 20 claimant or insurer shall immediately provide written notice 21 to the division, in the form and manner prescribed by the 22 division, and the division shall randomly select an umpire from 23 the umpire list and notify the parties. 24 d. If either appraiser requests that an umpire be selected 25 by a judge in the state in which the property that is the 26 subject of the claim is located, a judge shall give deference 27 to the randomly selected umpire from the umpire list by the 28 division unless either the claimant or the insurer provides 29 good cause for the judge to make an alternative selection from 30 the umpire list. 31 4. Within forty-five calendar days from the date the 32 umpire is selected, both appraisers shall appraise the loss, 33 stating separately the actual cash value and the amount of 34 loss for each item. Each appraiser shall submit separately 35 -72- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 72/ 106 S.F. 619 the appraiserâs actual cash value and amount of loss of each 1 item, along with any supporting information, to the umpire. 2 Each appraiser shall also submit written authorization for the 3 umpire to commence the umpireâs work. 4 5. No later than forty-five calendar days after receipt of 5 the actual cash value and amount of loss under subsection 4, 6 the umpire shall prepare and provide to the parties and each 7 appraiser a written itemized award showing the actual cash 8 value and amount of loss. The written itemized award shall 9 include but is not limited to all of the following: 10 a. Contact information for each appraiser and the umpire. 11 b. The insuredâs policy number and the insuredâs claim 12 number. 13 c. The date of the insuredâs loss. 14 d. The type of covered peril that caused the loss. 15 e. The date the umpire commenced work. 16 f. The legal name of the insurer. 17 g. The physical address of the property on which the insured 18 made a claim. 19 h. The date of the umpireâs written itemized award. 20 i. (1) A description and itemization of the final written 21 itemized award by coverage type, including but not limited to: 22 (a) Coverage A ââ dwelling. 23 (b) Coverage B ââ other structures. 24 (c) Coverage C ââ personal property. 25 (2) The description and itemization by coverage type shall 26 include contested items that have been resolved, sublimits, 27 and other disputed items. Items, including but not limited 28 to items with sublimits, shall be separately noted to avoid 29 ambiguity in the final written itemized award. 30 j. The signature of the umpire and at least one appraiser. 31 6. Prior to the umpire issuing the written itemized award, 32 the parties may agree to conclude the appraisal process when 33 the parties reach a final settlement. 34 Sec. 70. The insurer shall provide the 11 insured with an itemized and detailed written explanation of 12 the payment of the settlement, including an explanation of any 13 item that is specifically denied under the terms of the policy. 14 Unless otherwise agreed upon by the parties in writing, an 15 appraisal award shall be binding and paid by the insurer 16 within sixty calendar days of the written itemized award being 17 submitted to the insurer. 18 3. NEW SECTION . 522F.19 Hearings ââ service of 18 process, attendance of witnesses, and production of documents. 19 1. Whenever the commissioner believes that a person has 20 been engaged, or is engaging, in a violation of this chapter 21 or a rule adopted or an order issued under this chapter, and 22 that a proceeding by the commissioner would be in the public 23 interest, the commissioner shall issue and serve upon the 24 person a statement of the charges and a notice of a hearing on 25 the charges to be held at the time and place set in the notice, 26 which shall not be less than ten business days after the date 27 of service of such notice. 28 2. At the time and place of such hearing, the person shall 29 have an opportunity to be heard and to show cause why an order 30 should not be made by the commissioner requiring the person to 31 cease and desist from the violation of the chapter, rule, or 32 order. Upon a showing of good cause, the commissioner shall 33 permit any person, by counsel or in person, to intervene, 34 appear, and be heard at such hearing. 35 -75- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 75/ 106 S.F. 619 3. A hearing under this section shall not be required to 1 observe formal rules of pleading or evidence. 2 4. The commissioner, at a hearing under this section, may 3 administer oaths, examine and cross-examine witnesses, receive 4 oral and documentary evidence, and may subpoena witnesses, 5 compel their attendance, and require the production of books, 6 papers, records, correspondence, or other documents which the 7 commissioner deems relevant. The commissioner may, and upon 8 the request of any party shall, cause to be made a stenographic 9 record of the evidence and proceedings of a hearing under this 10 section. If no stenographic record is made and if a judicial 11 review is sought, the commissioner shall prepare a statement 12 of the evidence and proceeding for use on review. If a person 13 refuses to comply with a subpoena issued under this section, 14 or to testify to a matter for which the person may lawfully be 15 interrogated, the district court of Polk county or the district 16 court of the county where the person resides, on application of 17 the commissioner, may issue an order requiring such person to 18 comply with such subpoena or to testify. Failure of a person 19 to obey such order of the court may be punished by the court as 20 contempt. 21 5. Statements of charges, notices, orders, subpoenas, and 22 other processes of the commissioner under this chapter may be 23 served by anyone authorized by the commissioner, either in the 24 manner provided by law for service of process in civil actions, 25 or by mailing a copy by restricted certified mail to the person 26 affected by the statement, notice, order, subpoena, or other 27 process at the personâs residence or principal office or place 28 of business. The verified return by the person serving the 29 statement, notice, order, subpoena, or other process, setting 30 forth the manner of such service, shall be proof of service, 31 and the return receipt for the statement, notice, order, 32 subpoena, or other process, mailed by restricted certified 33 mail, shall be proof of the service. 34 Sec. 75. NEW SECTION . 522F.21 Civil and criminal penalties. 19 1. a. Upon a determination by the commissioner, after 20 a hearing conducted pursuant to chapter 17A, that a person 21 violated this chapter, the commissioner shall reduce the 22 findings of the hearing to writing and deliver a copy of the 23 findings to the person. 24 b. Upon a determination by the commissioner that a person 25 has engaged, is engaging, or is about to engage in any act or 26 practice constituting a violation of this chapter or a rule 27 adopted or order issued under this chapter, the commissioner 28 may take the following actions: 29 (1) Issue an order requiring the person to cease and desist 30 from engaging in the conduct resulting in the violation. 31 (2) Assess a civil penalty against the person of not more 32 than one thousand dollars for each violation not to exceed an 33 aggregate of ten thousand dollars. 34 (3) If the person knew or reasonably should have known the 35 -80- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 80/ 106 S.F. 619 person was in violation of this chapter, assess a civil penalty 1 of not more than five thousand dollars for each violation 2 of this chapter not to exceed an aggregate penalty of fifty 3 thousand dollars in any one six-month period. 4 (4) (a) Issue a summary order, including a brief statement 5 of findings of fact, conclusions of law, and policy reasons for 6 the decision, and directing the person to cease and desist from 7 engaging in the act or practice or to take affirmative action 8 as is necessary in the judgment of the commissioner to comply 9 with the requirements of this chapter. 10 (b) A person may contest a summary order by filing, 11 within thirty calendar days from the date of the issuance of 12 the summary order, a written request for a contested case 13 proceeding and hearing as provided in chapter 17A and in 14 accordance with rules adopted by the commissioner. Section 15 17A.18A shall be inapplicable to a summary order issued under 16 this subsection. If a hearing is not requested within thirty 17 calendar days from the date of issuance of the summary order, 18 the summary order shall become final by operation of law. A 19 summary order shall remain effective from the date of issuance 20 until the date the order becomes final by operation of law, 21 or is modified or overturned by a presiding officer or court 22 following a request for hearing. 23 (c) A person violating a summary order issued under this 24 subsection shall be deemed in contempt of the summary order. 25 The commissioner may petition the district court to enforce the 26 order as certified by the commissioner. The district court 27 shall find the person in contempt of the order if the court 28 finds, after conducting a hearing, that the person is not 29 in compliance with the order. The court may assess a civil 30 penalty against the person and may issue further orders as the 31 court deems appropriate. 32 c. In addition to any other penalty under this section, 33 if the commissioner finds that a violation of this chapter 34 was directed, encouraged, condoned, ignored, or ratified by 35 -81- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 81/ 106 S.F. 619 the employer of the appraiser or umpire, the commissioner 1 shall assess a penalty to the employer. Penalties under this 2 paragraph may be retained by the commissioner under the fund 3 described in section 505.7, subsection 9. 4 2. a. A person acting as an appraiser or an umpire without 5 proper licensure, or an appraiser or an umpire who willfully 6 violates any provision of this chapter or an order issued 7 under this chapter, is guilty of a class âDâ felony. If the 8 violation results in a loss of more than ten thousand dollars, 9 the appraiser or an umpire is guilty of a class âCâ felony. 10 b. The commissioner may refer such evidence as is available 11 concerning a violation of this chapter, or of any rule adopted 12 or order issued under this chapter, or of the failure of a 13 person to comply with the licensing requirements of this 14 chapter, to the attorney general or the proper district 15 attorney who may institute the appropriate criminal proceedings 16 under this chapter. 17 c. This chapter shall not limit the power of the state to 18 punish any person for any conduct that constitutes a crime 19 under any other statute. 20 Sec. 77. NEW SECTION . 522F.23 Suspension for failure to 17 pay child support or state debt. 18 1.
