EFFECTIVE DATE. This division of this Act, being 33 deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon enactment. 34 EXPLANATION 35 -90- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 90/ 106 S.F. 619 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with 1 the explanationâs substance by the members of the general assembly. 2 This bill relates to the natural hazard mitigation financing 3 program, the disaster recovery housing assistance program, the 4 disaster recovery new housing program, post-loss assignments 5 of benefits, and the licensing and regulation of adjusters, 6 appraisers and umpires. 7 DIVISION I ââ NATURAL HAZARD MITIGATION FINANCING PROGRAM. 8 The bill creates the natural hazard mitigation financing 9 program (program) for the purpose of making loans available 10 to eligible entities to finance all or part of the costs of a 11 project. âEligible entityâ and âprojectâ are defined in the 12 bill. The program shall be a joint and cooperative undertaking 13 of the department of homeland security and emergency management 14 (HSEMD) and the Iowa finance authority (IFA). 15 The bill creates a natural hazard mitigation revolving loan 16 fund (fund) under the control of HSEMD, in consultation with 17 IFA, consisting of moneys and program funding as detailed in 18 the bill. 19 HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, may establish and maintain 20 funds or accounts necessary to carry out the purposes of the 21 bill. Any moneys appropriated to HSEMD and IFA for purposes 22 of paying the costs and expenses associated with the program 23 shall be administered as determined by IFA. The funds or 24 accounts are separate dedicated funds and accounts under the 25 administration and control of IFA, and shall not be considered 26 part of the general fund of the state, are not subject to 27 appropriation for any other purpose by the general assembly, 28 and in determining a general fund balance shall not be included 29 in the general fund of the state, but shall remain in the funds 30 and accounts maintained by HSEMD or IFA. IFA may provide for 31 the issuance of bonds or notes as detailed in the bill. 32 The duties of the director of HSEMD (director) are detailed 33 in the bill. 34 For the fiscal year beginning July 1, 2025, and each fiscal 35 -91- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 91/ 106 S.F. 619 year thereafter, HSEMD may prepare and deliver intended use 1 plans to, and enter into capitalization grant agreements with, 2 the administrator of the United States federal emergency 3 management agency and may accept capitalization grants for the 4 fund. HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, shall establish fiscal 5 controls and accounting procedures for the fund. 6 HSEMD and IFA shall review each loan application to 7 determine if the applicant is an eligible entity and qualifies 8 for a loan. IFA, in cooperation with HSEMD, shall determine 9 the interest rate and repayment terms for each loan under the 10 program and shall enter into a loan agreement with each loan 11 recipient. IFA may charge loan recipients fees and assess 12 costs as necessary. 13 Moneys in the fund shall be used for the primary purpose of 14 making loans to eligible entities to finance eligible costs of 15 projects in accordance with the intended use plans. The loan 16 recipients and the purpose and amount of the loans shall be 17 determined by the director. 18 HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, shall adopt rules pursuant 19 to Code chapter 17A to administer the division of the bill. 20 The bill makes a conforming change to Code section 422.7. 21 DIVISION II ââ DISASTER RECOVERY HOUSING ASSISTANCE PROGRAM. 22 The bill requires a state of disaster emergency proclamation 23 by the governor that authorizes disaster recovery housing 24 assistance to specify if disaster recovery housing assistance 25 is available to homeowners, renters, or both homeowners and 26 renters. 27 The bill defines âfinancial assistanceâ as assistance 28 provided only from the funds, rights, and assets legally 29 available to IFA and includes but is not limited to assistance 30 in the form of grants, loans, and forgivable loans. 31 Under the bill, IFA shall not use more than 5 percent of the 32 moneys deposited into the disaster recovery housing assistance 33 fund for administrative and program costs. 34 Under current law, to be considered for financial assistance 35 -92- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 92/ 106 S.F. 619 under the disaster recovery housing assistance program, 1 a homeowner or renter must register for the disaster case 2 advocacy program. Under the bill, a homeowner or renter is not 3 required to register for the advocacy program to be considered 4 for financial assistance under the disaster recovery housing 5 assistance program. 6 The bill makes conforming changes to Code section 16.57B. 7 DIVISION III ââ DISASTER RECOVERY NEW HOUSING PROGRAM. The 8 bill defines âqualifying state disaster recovery new housing 9 grantâ (grant) as an award of a state disaster recovery new 10 housing grant that was applied for between August 20, 2024, 11 and December 31, 2024, and approved and issued by the economic 12 development authority. A grant shall not be included in the 13 computation of net income for federal income tax purposes. 14 Code section 422.7, subsection 45, and Code section 422.35, 15 subsection 14, are repealed January 1, 2028. 16 The division takes effect upon enactment and applies 17 retroactively to tax years beginning on or after January 1, 18 2024. 19 DIVISION IV ââ POST-LOSS ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS ââ 20 RESIDENTIAL CONTRACTOR. Under the bill, a violation of Code 21 section 515.137 is an unfair method of competition and unfair 22 or deceptive act or practice in the business of insurance. 23 The bill defines âpost-loss assignmentâ (assignment). The 24 assignment must only assign the insurance proceeds a named 25 insured is entitled to receive from the named insuredâs insurer 26 for the repair, replacement construction, or reconstruction of 27 the named insuredâs property. 28 A residential contractor (contractor) shall not engage 29 in conduct prohibited by the bill under an assignment by a 30 named insured to the contractor under a property and casualty 31 insurance policy. 32 An assignment must include an itemized description 33 containing the information detailed in the bill. 34 An assignment shall not impair the interest of a mortgagee, 35 -93- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 93/ 106 S.F. 619 and all mortgagees shall be named as a co-payee for the payment 1 of benefits. An assignment shall only authorize a contractor 2 to be named as a co-payee, along with the named insured and all 3 mortgagees, for the payment of benefits. An assignment shall 4 not prevent or inhibit an insurer from communicating with the 5 named insured or a mortgagee. 6 An electronic copy of a fully executed assignment shall 7 be provided to a named insured and all mortgagees of the 8 damaged residential real estate within five business days after 9 execution. A contractor named in an assignment must cooperate 10 with the insurer in a claim investigation. 11 A named insured shall have the right to cancel an assignment 12 without penalty or fee under the circumstances detailed in the 13 bill. 14 Any written contract, repair estimate, or work order 15 prepared by a contractor to provide goods or services pursuant 16 to an assignment shall include notice as provided in the bill 17 which shall be signed by the named insured and sent to the 18 named insuredâs insurer prior to payment. 19 For at least 72 hours following a catastrophic disaster, a 20 residential contractor shall not enter into a contract with 21 an insured that includes an assignment. If the severity of 22 the catastrophic disaster has placed people under duress, as 23 determined by the commissioner, the commissioner shall dispatch 24 the consumer advocate and personnel to provide consumer 25 guidance. The commissioner may extend the 72-hour period by an 26 additional 72 hours after public hearing. 27 An assignment entered into with a contractor shall be void if 28 the contractor violates the bill. 29 DIVISION V ââ PUBLIC, INDEPENDENT, AND STAFF ADJUSTERS. The 30 bill makes conforming changes to Code sections 522B.5A and 31 522C.1. 32 Under current law, the commissioner of insurance 33 (commissioner) shall adopt rules as necessary to administer and 34 enforce Code chapter 522C. Under the bill, the commissioner 35 -94- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 94/ 106 S.F. 619 may adopt such rules. 1 Under the bill, a person shall not act as, or represent that 2 the person is, a public adjuster or an independent adjuster 3 unless the person is licensed. A license as an adjuster is 4 not required for a staff adjuster, an attorney when acting 5 within their professional capacity as an attorney, or a person 6 employed only for the purpose of obtaining facts surrounding a 7 loss or to furnish technical assistance to a licensed adjuster. 8 A person applying for an adjuster license shall complete an 9 application as described in the bill. The commissioner may 10 require a criminal history check for the applicant. 11 Prior to approving an application for a resident adjuster 12 license, a nonresident adjuster license, or a business entityâs 13 or nonresident business entityâs application for a license for 14 a resident public adjuster or resident independent adjuster, 15 the commissioner shall find that the applicant meets the 16 requirements detailed in the bill. 17 If the commissioner does not renew a license or denies 18 an application for a license, the commissioner shall notify 19 the applicant or licensee and advise of the reason for the 20 nonrenewal or denial. Within 30 calendar days of the date of 21 the notice, the licensee or applicant may request a hearing on 22 the nonrenewal or denial. 23 Application fees for a license as an adjuster are detailed 24 in the bill. The fee for an examination may be set by a 25 third-party testing service and must be approved by the 26 division of insurance (division). 27 Prior to issuance of a license, an applicant shall secure 28 evidence of financial responsibility (responsibility) through 29 a surety bond (bond) as prescribed by the commissioner. The 30 bond shall be executed and issued by an insurer authorized 31 to issue bonds, and must meet the requirements of the 32 bill. The division may request that an adjuster provide 33 evidence of responsibility at any time. An adjuster shall 34 immediately notify the division if the adjusterâs evidence 35 -95- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 95/ 106 S.F. 619 of responsibility terminates or becomes impaired, and the 1 adjusterâs license shall become inactive. 2 An individual applying for a license shall pass a written 3 examination, unless exempt, as described in the bill. An 4 individual who concurrently applies for an adjuster license and 5 an appraiser license may choose to take a joint examination as 6 detailed in the bill. An individual who successfully passes a 7 joint examination and meets the licensure requirements shall be 8 licensed as both an adjuster and an appraiser. 9 A public adjuster shall not provide services to an insured 10 until a written contract with the insured has been executed. 11 The contract must meet all of the requirements detailed in the 12 bill. No provisions in the contract shall be redacted in a 13 copy of the contract submitted to the commissioner. 14 If the insurer, no later than five calendar days after the 15 date on which the insuredâs loss is reported, either pays 16 or commits in writing to pay the policy limits, the public 17 adjuster shall inform the insured that the total amount of 18 loss claimed by the insured may not be paid by the insured, 19 and the adjuster is only entitled to reasonable compensation 20 from the insured. Prior to execution of a contract, the public 21 adjuster shall review the terms of the contract with the 22 insured and provide a separate disclosure document that meets 23 the requirements detailed in the bill. 24 An original copy of a completed contract shall be provided 25 to the public adjuster and kept by the insured. A contract 26 may be executed electronically if done so in compliance with 27 Code chapter 554D. Within 72 hours of entering a contract with 28 an insured, the public adjuster shall provide the insuredâs 29 insurer a notification letter. A contract between a public 30 adjuster and an insured executed in violation of the bill shall 31 not be enforceable. 32 The required standards of conduct for, and duties of, an 33 adjuster are detailed in the bill. An adjuster who fails 34 to comply with the standards and duties shall be subject to 35 -96- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 96/ 106 S.F. 619 penalties. 1 The division may place on probation, suspend, revoke, or 2 refuse to issue or renew an adjusterâs license, and may levy 3 a civil penalty for any of the reasons enumerated in the 4 bill. If the commissioner does not renew a license or denies 5 an application for a license, the commissioner shall notify 6 the adjuster or applicant and advise of the reason for the 7 nonrenewal or denial. The adjuster or applicant may request a 8 hearing within 30 days from the date of the notice. 9 The commissioner may conduct an investigation of any 10 suspected violation of the bill and may impose a penalty or 11 remedy against any person who is under investigation for, or 12 charged with, a violation even if the personâs license has been 13 surrendered or has lapsed by operation of law. 14 All complaint files, investigation files, other 15 investigation reports, and other investigative information in 16 the possession of the commissioner that relates to adjuster 17 discipline are privileged and confidential, and may only be 18 disclosed as described in the bill. On appeal by the adjuster, 19 the commissioner shall transmit the entire record of the 20 contested case to the reviewing court. 21 Upon a determination by the commissioner, after a hearing, 22 that an adjuster has violated a provision of the bill, 23 the commissioner shall reduce the findings of the hearing 24 to writing and deliver a copy to the adjuster. Upon a 25 determination by the commissioner that an adjuster has engaged 26 in any act or practice constituting a violation of the bill, 27 the commissioner may take any of the civil actions described 28 in the bill. 29 A person acting as an adjuster without proper licensure, 30 or an adjuster who willfully violates any provision of, or 31 order issued under, Code chapter 522C is guilty of a class 32 âDâ felony. When the violation results in a loss of more 33 than $10,000, the person or adjuster is guilty of a class âCâ 34 felony. 35 -97- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 97/ 106 S.F. 619 An adjuster who steals, converts, or misappropriates funds 1 that should be held in trust in a fiduciary capacity is guilty 2 of a class âDâ felony. When the violation results in a loss 3 of more than $10,000, the adjuster is guilty of a class âCâ 4 felony. 5 A class âDâ felony is punishable by confinement for no more 6 than five years and a fine of at least $1,025 but not more than 7 $10,245. A class âCâ felony is punishable by confinement for 8 no more than 10 years and a fine of at least $1,370 but not more 9 than $13,660. 10 The commissioner may refer evidence concerning violations of 11 the bill to the attorney general or the county attorney who may 12 institute criminal proceedings. 13 Any contract that is entered into by an insured with a person 14 who is not a licensed public adjuster shall be void, and the 15 insured is not liable for the payment of any past or future 16 services by the person under that contract or otherwise. 17 An adjuster whose license has been revoked or suspended, 18 or who forfeited a license, may apply to the commissioner for 19 reinstatement or reissuance and submit to a criminal history 20 check. An applicant shall not be eligible for reinstatement 21 or reissuance until the applicant satisfies the requirements 22 detailed in the bill. 23 An application for reinstatement or reissuance shall allege 24 facts as required by the bill, and the burden of proof is on 25 the adjuster to establish such facts. An adjuster may request 26 reinstatement of a suspended license prior to the end of the 27 suspension term. If an order of revocation or suspension did 28 not establish terms on which reinstatement or reissuance may 29 occur, or if the license was forfeited, an initial application 30 for reinstatement or reissuance shall not be made until at 31 least one year from the date of the order. All proceedings on 32 the application for reinstatement or reissuance shall be held 33 in accordance with Code chapter 17A. 34 If an adjusterâs ordered suspension period ends prior to 35 -98- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 98/ 106 S.F. 619 the adjusterâs license expiration date, and the adjuster 1 applies for reinstatement and meets all requirements, the 2 division shall reinstate the license as soon as practicable 3 but no earlier than the end of the suspension period. If an 4 adjusterâs license is suspended beyond the adjusterâs license 5 expiration date, the adjuster must apply for reissuance. A 6 submission of voluntary forfeiture of a license shall be made 7 to the commissioner pursuant to the requirements detailed in 8 the bill. 9 The commissioner may deny an application for reinstatement 10 or reissuance, or bring an additional immediate action, if an 11 adjuster has engaged in an additional violation of Code chapter 12 507B or 522C. 13 The commissioner shall deny an adjusterâs application for 14 license issuance, renewal, reinstatement, or reissuance; 15 suspend a current license; or revoke a currently suspended 16 license, upon receipt of a certificate of noncompliance from 17 the child support recovery unit or the centralized collection 18 unit of the department of revenue. 19 The license and examination requirements of Code chapter 20 522C in this division of the bill apply three months after 21 the enactment date of this division of the bill to a person 22 currently doing business as an independent or staff adjuster 23 as of January 1, 2025. 24 DIVISION VI ââ LICENSING AND REGULATION OF APPRAISERS 25 AND UMPIRES. Under the bill, the commissioner may require a 26 criminal history check on an applicant that applies for an 27 initial license as an appraiser, or an umpire; or a renewal, 28 reinstatement, or reissuance of a license if the license of 29 an appraiser or an umpire has been revoked or suspended. The 30 commissioner may adopt rules to administer this division of the 31 bill. 32 Under the bill, a person shall not act as, or represent that 33 the person is, an appraiser or an umpire unless the person is 34 licensed. 35 -99- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 99/ 106 S.F. 619 A person applying for an appraiser or umpire license shall 1 submit an application prescribed by the commissioner. To be 2 eligible for licensure under the bill, a person shall meet all 3 of the criteria detailed in the bill. A person who meets the 4 requirements for licensure, unless otherwise denied licensure 5 pursuant to the bill, shall be issued an appraiser license or 6 an umpire license that is valid for two years. Applicable fees 7 are detailed in the bill. 8 An individual who concurrently applies for an adjuster 9 license and an appraiser license may choose to take a joint 10 examination as detailed in the bill. An individual who 11 successfully passes a joint examination and meets the licensure 12 requirements shall be licensed as both an adjuster and an 13 appraiser. 14 An appraiserâs license and an umpireâs license shall contain 15 the information described in the bill. An appraiser and an 16 umpire shall be required to complete continuing education 17 requirements, as prescribed by the division, to be eligible for 18 license renewal or reinstatement. 19 An appraiser and an umpire shall inform the division of a 20 change of legal name or business address within 30 calendar 21 days of the change. Failure to timely inform the division may 22 result in a penalty. 23 The division shall publish an appraiser list and an umpire 24 list on the divisionâs internet site, and include all required 25 information as detailed in the bill. 26 Prior to approving a business entityâs application for a 27 license as an appraiser, the commissioner shall find that the 28 business entity has designated an individual appraiser to be 29 responsible for the business entityâs compliance with the 30 insurance laws and rules. 31 An appraiser or an umpire may apply for reinstatement of an 32 expired license up to one year after the license expiration 33 date by meeting the requirements of the bill. An appraiser or 34 an umpire who fails to apply for license reinstatement within 35 -100- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 100/ 106 S.F. 619 one year must apply for a new license. An appraiser or an 1 umpire who surrendered a license and stated an intent to exit 2 the appraiser business may file a request to reactivate the 3 license within 90 calendar days of the date the license was 4 placed on inactive status. 5 Each party to an appraisal shall be responsible for the 6 partyâs own appraiserâs fees and expenses, an equal share of 7 all reasonable and necessary fees and expenses incurred by an 8 umpire, and an equal share of all reasonable and necessary 9 costs incurred in the course of conducting the appraisal. An 10 appraiser or an umpire shall not charge any party on a basis 11 dependent on the outcome of the written itemized award, or 12 charge in a manner that relies on a barter arrangement, gift, 13 favor, or in-kind exchange. Prior to the conclusion of an 14 appraisal process, an appraiser or umpire shall not require, 15 demand, or accept any fee unless the loss is being handled 16 by the appraiser or umpire on a time-plus-expense basis. An 17 appraiser or umpire shall not charge a fee if the appraiser or 18 umpire abandons the appraisal prior to the umpire issuing a 19 written itemized award. 20 The required standards of conduct for, and duties of, an 21 appraiser and an umpire are detailed in the bill. An appraiser 22 or umpire who fails to comply with the standards and duties 23 shall be subject to penalties. 24 The process for an appraisal is detailed in the bill. The 25 claimant and the insurer must both provide the other party with 26 a list stating separately the actual cash value and the amount 27 of claimed loss for each item at issue. Within 20 calendar 28 days of receipt of a written demand for an appraisal, the 29 claimant and the insurer shall each select an appraiser from 30 the appraiser list. Upon selection, the appraiser shall attest 31 that the appraiser is competent and disinterested with regards 32 to the appraisal. 33 Within 15 calendar days of the selection of appraisers, both 34 appraisers shall agree on an umpire from the umpire list. A 35 -101- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 101/ 106 S.F. 619 party or an appraiser may object to the umpire for good cause 1 no later than five business days after the umpire has been 2 selected. A replacement umpire shall then be selected by both 3 appraisers from the umpire list. If both appraisers fail to 4 agree on an umpire, the division shall randomly select an 5 umpire from the umpire list and notify the parties. If either 6 appraiser requests that an umpire be selected by a judge, a 7 judge shall give deference to the randomly selected umpire from 8 the umpire list by the division unless either the claimant 9 or the insurer provides good cause for the judge to make an 10 alternative selection. 11 Within 45 calendar days from the date the umpire is 12 selected, both appraisers shall appraise the loss and submit 13 the appraiserâs actual cash value and amount of loss of each 14 item to the umpire. Each appraiser shall also submit written 15 authorization for the umpire to commence work. No later than 16 45 calendar days after receipt of the actual cash value and 17 amount of loss, the umpire shall prepare and provide to the 18 parties and each appraiser a written itemized award showing the 19 actual cash value and amount of loss. 20 All property insurance policies delivered, issued for 21 delivery, continued, or renewed in this state on or after 22 January 1, 2026, shall contain an appraisal clause that 23 complies with the bill. 24 An appraiser and umpire shall act with due diligence in 25 achieving an appraisal award. An insurerâs payment of an 26 appraisal award to an insured shall be subject to applicable 27 policy terms and conditions, limits, and deductibles. The 28 insurer shall provide the insured with a written explanation of 29 the payment of the settlement, including an explanation of any 30 item that is specifically denied under the terms of the policy. 31 Unless otherwise agreed on by the parties, an appraisal award 32 shall be binding and paid by the insurer within 60 calendar 33 days of the award being submitted to the insurer. 34 An appraiser or umpire shall report to the commissioner any 35 -102- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 102/ 106 S.F. 619 administrative action taken against the appraiser or umpire 1 within 30 calendar days of the final disposition. Within 2 30 calendar days of the initial pretrial hearing date, an 3 appraiser or umpire shall report to the commissioner any 4 criminal prosecution of the appraiser or umpire. An appraiser 5 or umpire who willfully fails to comply with such requirements 6 is subject to penalty. 7 An appraiser or umpire has a continuing duty and obligation 8 to keep usual and customary records pertaining to appraisals 9 in accordance with the requirements of the bill. An appraiser 10 or umpire who willfully fails to comply with such requirements 11 is subject to penalty. 12 Whenever the commissioner believes that a person has been 13 engaged or is engaging in a violation of the bill, and that a 14 proceeding by the commissioner would be in the public interest, 15 the commissioner shall issue and serve a statement of the 16 charges and a notice of a hearing. 17 The division may place on probation, suspend, revoke, 18 or refuse to issue or renew an appraiserâs license or an 19 umpireâs license, and may levy a civil penalty for any of 20 the causes detailed in the bill. The commissioner may 2 conduct an investigation and may enforce the provisions of the 3 bill. 4 All investigative information in the possession of the 5 commissioner that relates to appraiser or umpire discipline 6 is privileged and confidential, and may only be disclosed as 7 described in the bill. On appeal by the appraiser or umpire, 8 the commissioner shall transmit the entire record of the 9 contested case to the reviewing court. Upon a determination by 10 the commissioner, after hearing, that an appraiser or umpire 11 has violated a provision of the bill, the commissioner shall 12 reduce the findings of the hearing to writing and deliver 13 a copy of the findings to the appraiser or umpire, and the 14 commissioner may take any of the actions described in the bill. 15 A person acting as an appraiser or an umpire without proper 16 licensure, or an appraiser or an umpire who willfully violates 17 any provision of, or an order issued under, the bill is guilty 18 of a class âDâ felony. When the violation results in a loss of 19 more than $10,000, the person or adjuster is guilty of a class 20 âCâ felony. 21 A class âDâ felony is punishable by confinement for no more 22 than five years and a fine of at least $1,025 but not more than 23 $10,245. A class âCâ felony is punishable by confinement for 24 no more than 10 years and a fine of at least $1,370 but not more 25 than $13,660. 26 The commissioner may refer such evidence concerning 27 violations of the bill, or of the failure of a person to comply 28 with the licensing requirements under the bill, to the attorney 29 general or the district attorney who may institute criminal 30 proceedings. 31 An appraiser or an umpire whose license has been revoked or 32 suspended by order, or who forfeited a license, may apply to 33 the commissioner for reinstatement or reissuance, and submit to 34 a criminal history check. 35 -104- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 104/ 106 S.F. 619 All proceedings on the application for reinstatement or 1 reissuance shall be held in accordance with Code chapter 17A. 2 An order of reinstatement or reissuance shall be based on a 3 written decision, and may impose such terms and conditions as 4 the commissioner deems appropriate. 5 If an appraiserâs or an umpireâs ordered suspension period 6 ends prior to the appraiserâs or umpireâs license expiration 7 date and the adjuster applies for reinstatement and meets all 8 applicable requirements, the division shall reinstate the 9 license as soon as practicable but no earlier than the end 10 of the suspension period. PROPERTY INSURANCE POLICIES OBLIGATE THE INSURED TO 1 PRESENT A CLAIM TO THE INSUREDâS INSURER FOR CONSIDERATION. 2 THERE ARE THREE TYPES OF ADJUSTERS THAT MAY BE INVOLVED IN THAT 3 PROCESS. THEY WILL NOT 6 CHARGE THE INSURED A FEE. 7 (B) âINDEPENDENT ADJUSTERâ IS DEFINED IN IOWA CODE SECTION 8 522C.2. AN INDEPENDENT ADJUSTER IS CONTRACTED BY THE INSURER 9 TO REPRESENT THE INSURER. THEY WILL NOT CHARGE THE INSURED A 10 FEE. 11 (C) âPUBLIC ADJUSTERâ IS DEFINED IN IOWA CODE SECTION 12 522C.2. A PUBLIC ADJUSTER IS NOT AN EMPLOYEE OR REPRESENTATIVE 13 OF THE INSURER. THEY ARE HIRED BY THE INSURED TO ASSIST IN THE 14 PREPARATION, PRESENTATION, AND SETTLEMENT OF A CLAIM. 15 2. THE INSURED IS NOT REQUIRED TO HIRE A PUBLIC ADJUSTER 16 TO HELP THE INSURED MEET THE INSUREDâS OBLIGATIONS UNDER THE 17 INSUREDâS POLICY, BUT HAS THE RIGHT TO DO SO. 18 3. THE INSURED MAY BE RESPONSIBLE FOR ANY AMOUNT PAYABLE TO 24 A PUBLIC ADJUSTER RELATED TO ANY PORTION OF A CLAIM THAT WAS 25 PREVIOUSLY PAID IN PART, IN FULL, OR SETTLED BY THE INSURER 26 PRIOR TO A CONTRACT BEING ENTERED INTO BETWEEN THE PUBLIC 27 ADJUSTER AND THE INSURED. 28 5. NEW SECTION . 522C.11 Adjusters ââ standards of 16 conduct. 17 1. A public adjuster shall serve with objectivity and 18 complete loyalty to the interest of the insured. A public 19 adjuster shall render to the insured in good faith information, 20 counsel, and service, that in the opinion of the public 21 adjuster will best serve the insuredâs insurance claim needs 22 and interest. These duties extend to the claims process and 23 include providing timely responses to both the insurer and the 24 insured. 25 2. For a minimum of seventy-two hours following a 26 catastrophic disaster, to allow time for the commissioner 27 to safely deploy consumer protection resources, a public 28 adjuster shall not, in person or by telephone, directly offer 29 to contract, attempt to offer to contract, or enter into an 30 adjuster contract with an insured unless the offer to contract, 31 the attempt to offer to contract, or entering into a contract 32 is initiated by a consumer. If the commissioner deems the 33 severity of the catastrophic disaster to have placed people 34 under duress, the commissioner shall immediately dispatch the 35 -38- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 38/ 106 S.F. 619 consumer advocate and other personnel to the disaster area to 1 provide consumer guidance. If, after a public hearing, the 2 commissioner determines that, due to the scope and severity 3 of the catastrophic disaster, additional time is necessary to 4 safely deploy additional consumer protection resources, the 5 commissioner may extend the time period that a public adjuster 6 shall not offer to contract, attempt to offer to contract, or 7 enter into a contract for an additional seventy-two hours. 8 3. A public adjuster shall not solicit between the hours 9 of 8:00 p.m. and 9:00 a.m. Solicitation shall include but is 10 not limited to a door-to-door sale as that term is defined in 11 section 555A.1. 12 4. A public adjuster, or an independent adjuster, shall not 13 permit an unlicensed employee or representative of the public 14 adjuster or independent adjuster, nor any person associated 15 with a claim, to conduct business for which a license is 16 required under this chapter. 17 5. An adjuster shall not have a direct or indirect financial 18 interest in any aspect of a claim other than the amount payable 19 pursuant to the written contract with an insured under section 20 522C.10. 21 6. An adjuster shall not acquire any interest in salvage of 22 property. 23 7. An adjuster shall not undertake the adjustment of any 24 claim if the adjuster is not competent and knowledgeable as 25 to the terms and conditions of the insurance coverage, or if 26 the loss or coverage otherwise exceeds the adjusterâs current 27 expertise. 28 8. An adjuster shall maintain all documentation relating to 29 all estimates and coverage determinations for a minimum of five 30 years from the date of completion of a settlement. 31 9. An adjuster shall not knowingly make any false oral or 32 written material statements regarding any person engaged in the 33 business of insurance, or any other adjuster, to an insured who 34 is a client or potential client. 35 -39- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 39/ 106 S.F. 619 10. a. An adjuster shall not reasonably act, or fail to 1 act, in any manner that obstructs or prevents an insurer or 2 adjuster from timely conducting an inspection of any part of 3 an insuredâs property for which there is a claim for loss or 4 damage. 5 b. If a public adjuster is unavailable after reasonable 6 request by an insurer, resulting in delay of the insurerâs 7 timely inspection of the property, the insured shall allow 8 the insurer to have access to the property without the 9 participation or presence of the public adjuster to facilitate 10 the insurerâs prompt inspection of the loss or damage. 11 11. An adjuster shall respond to an inquiry from an insurer 12 or an insured regarding a claim within fifteen business days 13 of the date of the inquiry unless good cause exists for delay. 14 The adjuster shall reply within fifteen business days to all 15 pertinent communications from the insured, the insurer, or a 16 representative of the insured or the insurer that reasonably 17 suggest that a response is expected. 18 12. Upon receiving notification of a claim, an insurer shall 19 provide necessary claim forms, instructions, and reasonable 20 assistance within fifteen business days of notification of the 21 claim so that first-party claimants can comply with the policy 22 conditions and the insurerâs reasonable requirements. 23 13. An adjuster shall not act as an appraiser and as an 24 adjuster on the same claim. 25 14. An adjuster shall not act as an umpire and as an 26 adjuster on the same claim. 27 15. A public adjuster shall not enter into a contract that 28 accepts a power of attorney or limited power of attorney for 29 an insured. 30 16. a. An independent adjuster shall not act as an 31 independent adjuster and a public adjuster on the same claim. 32 b. A public adjuster shall not act as a public adjuster and 33 an independent adjuster on the same claim. 34 17. A staff adjuster may be licensed as a public adjuster 35 -40- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 40/ 106 S.F. 619 or as an independent adjuster, but shall be prohibited from 1 providing services as an independent adjuster or a public 2 adjuster while employed as a staff adjuster. 3 18. A public adjuster shall not agree to, or reject, any 4 loss settlement without the insuredâs express knowledge and 5 written consent. 6 19. An adjuster shall not engage in any act or practice 7 that is a conflict of interest. A conflict of interest shall 8 include but is not limited to the following: 9 a. A direct or indirect financial interest with a person 10 responsible for the reconstruction, repair, or restoration of 11 damaged property that is the subject of a claim, or with a 12 person involved in resolving a claim valuation dispute. 13 b. A direct or indirect financial interest, or other 14 valuable consideration regardless of form or amount paid to an 15 adjuster in exchange for referring an insured to an appraiser, 16 umpire, construction company, contractor, salvage company, or 17 attorney. 18 c. Being an owner, employee, agent, investor, or having 19 other financial interest in a business entity responsible for 20 the reconstruction, repair, or restoration of damaged property 21 that is the subject of a claim, or having an immediate family 22 member who is an owner, employee, agent, or investor in a 23 business entity responsible for the reconstruction, repair, 24 or restoration of a damaged property that is the subject of a 25 claim. 26 d. Entering into a written or verbal contract, or formal 27 or informal agreement, with any person that compromises the 28 adjusterâs duty of loyalty to the insured. 29 e. Using claim information obtained in the course of a claim 30 investigation for commercial purposes including marketing or 31 advertising for the benefit of the adjuster. 32 20. A public adjuster shall not file a complaint with 33 the division on behalf of an insured without the insuredâs 34 knowledge and written consent. 35 -41- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 41/ 106 S.F. 619 21. An adjuster shall not represent, directly or 1 indirectly, that damage has occurred at a property unless the 2 adjuster has inspected the damaged areas of the property. 3 22. An adjuster shall produce a detailed written estimate to 4 repair or replace covered damages and provide a copy to both 5 the insured and the insurer in a timely manner. 6 23. A public adjuster shall not offer to pay an insuredâs 7 deductible, or claim that the insuredâs deductible will be 8 waived, as an inducement to use the services of the public 9 adjuster. 10 24. An adjuster shall respond reasonably promptly to 11 inquiries by the division. 12 25. A public adjuster shall provide a detailed invoice for 13 completed services to an insured prior to requesting payment 14 for services pursuant to a contract under section 522C.10. 15 26. Funds received or held by a public adjuster on behalf of 16 an insured toward the settlement of a claim shall be: 17 a. Held in a fiduciary capacity. 18 b. Deposited by the adjuster into one or more separate 19 noninterest-bearing fiduciary trust accounts in a financial 20 institution licensed to do business in this state no later 21 than the close of the fifth business day from the date the 22 public adjuster received the funds, and either deposited in the 23 insuredâs name or in the name of the public adjuster as trustee 24 for the insured, to be held and administered as a trust account 25 for the benefit and protection of the insured. 26 c. Listed specifically and separately, by the insuredâs name 29 and the amount in trust in the book of accounts and records of 30 the public adjuster. Disbursed within thirty calendar days of receipt of an 34 invoice by the public adjuster from a contractor that completed 35 -42- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 42/ 106 S.F. 619 work, if the public adjuster receives approval of the insured 1 that the work was satisfactorily completed. 2 27. A public adjuster shall comply with all applicable local 3 ordinances. 4 28. NEW SECTION . 522C.14 Civil and criminal penalties. 31 1. a. Upon a determination by the commissioner after a 32 hearing conducted pursuant to chapter 17A that an adjuster has 33 violated a provision of this chapter, the commissioner shall 34 reduce the findings of the hearing to writing and deliver a 35 -46- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 46/ 106 S.F. 619 copy of the findings to the adjuster. 1 b. Upon a determination by the commissioner that an adjuster 2 has engaged, is engaging, or is about to engage in any act or 3 practice constituting a violation of this chapter or a rule 4 adopted or order issued under this chapter, the commissioner 5 may take the following actions: 6 (1) Issue an order requiring the adjuster to cease and 7 desist from engaging in the conduct resulting in the violation. 8 (2) Assess a civil penalty against the adjuster of not more 9 than one thousand dollars for each violation of this chapter, 10 not to exceed an aggregate of ten thousand dollars. 11 (3) If the adjuster knew or reasonably should have known 12 the adjuster was in violation of this chapter, assess a 13 civil penalty of not more than five thousand dollars for each 14 violation of this chapter, not to exceed an aggregate penalty 15 of fifty thousand dollars in any one six-month period. 16 (4) (a) Issue a summary order, including a brief statement 17 of findings of fact, conclusions of law, and policy reasons for 18 the decision, and directing the adjuster to cease and desist 19 from engaging in the act or practice or to take affirmative 20 action as is necessary in the judgment of the commissioner to 21 comply with the requirements of this chapter. 22 (b) An adjuster may contest a summary order by filing, 23 within thirty calendar days from the date of the issuance of 24 the summary order, a written request for a contested case 25 proceeding and hearing as provided in chapter 17A and in 26 accordance with rules adopted by the commissioner. Section 27 17A.18A shall be inapplicable to a summary order issued under 28 this subsection. If a hearing is not requested within thirty 29 calendar days from the date of issuance of the summary order, 30 the summary order shall become final by operation of law. A 31 summary order shall remain effective from the date of issuance 32 until the date the order becomes final by operation of law, 33 or is modified or overturned by a presiding officer or court 34 following a request for hearing. 35 -47- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 47/ 106 S.F. 619 (c) An adjuster violating a summary order issued under this 1 subsection shall be deemed in contempt of the summary order. 2 The commissioner may petition the district court to enforce the 3 order as certified by the commissioner. The district court 4 shall find the adjuster in contempt of the order if the court 5 finds, after conducting a hearing, that the adjuster is not 6 in compliance with the order. The court may assess a civil 7 penalty against the adjuster and may issue further orders as 8 the court deems appropriate. 9 c. In addition to any other penalty under this section, 10 if the commissioner finds that a violation of this chapter 11 was directed, encouraged, condoned, ignored, or ratified by 12 the employer of the adjuster, the commissioner shall assess a 13 penalty to the employer. Penalties under this paragraph may be 14 retained by the commissioner under section 505.7, subsection 9. 15 2. a. A person acting as an adjuster without proper 16 licensure, or an adjuster who willfully violates any provision 17 of this chapter or an order issued under this chapter, is 18 guilty of a class âDâ felony. If the violation results in a 19 loss of more than ten thousand dollars, the person or adjuster 20 is guilty of a class âCâ felony. 21 b. An adjuster who steals, converts, or misappropriates 22 funds that should be held in trust under section 522C.11, is 23 guilty of a class âDâ felony. If the violation results in a 24 loss of more than ten thousand dollars, the adjuster is guilty 25 of a class âCâ felony. 26 c. The commissioner may refer such evidence as is available 27 concerning a violation of this chapter, or of any rule adopted 28 or order issued under this chapter, or of the failure of a 29 person to comply with the licensing requirements of this 30 chapter, to the attorney general or the proper county attorney 31 who may institute the appropriate criminal proceedings under 32 this chapter. 33 d. This chapter does not limit the power of the state to 34 punish any person for conduct that constitutes a crime under 35 -48- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 48/ 106 S.F. 619 any other statute. 1 3. Any contract regulated by this chapter that is entered 2 into by an insured with a person who is not a licensed public 3 adjuster in this state shall be void. If a contract is void, 4 the insured is not liable for the payment for any past services 5 rendered, or future services to be rendered, by that person. 6 Sec. 49. NEW SECTION . 522F.6 Appraisers ââ payment. 1 1. Each party to an appraisal shall be responsible for the 2 following: 3 a. The partyâs own appraiserâs fees and expenses. 4 b. An equal share of all reasonable and necessary fees and 5 expenses incurred by an umpire, if necessary. 6 c. An equal share of all reasonable and necessary costs 7 incurred in the course of conducting the appraisal. 8 2. a. An appraiser shall not charge any party on a basis 9 dependent on the outcome of the written itemized award, or 10 charge in a manner that relies on a barter arrangement, gift, 11 favor, or in-kind exchange. 12 b. Prior to the conclusion of an appraisal process via 13 final settlement or issuance of a written itemized award by 14 an umpire, an appraiser shall not require, demand, or accept 15 any fee, retainer, compensation, deposit, or other type 16 of consideration, unless the loss is being handled by the 17 appraiser on a time-plus-expense basis. 18 3. NEW SECTION . 522F.7 Appraisers ââ standards of 23 conduct. 24 1. An appraiser shall act with due diligence, including but 25 not limited to demonstrating accuracy, fairness, and timeliness 26 throughout an appraisal process. 27 2. a. (1) No later than five business days after being 28 hired by a party to an appraisal and before beginning work as 29 an appraiser, an appraiser shall disclose to all parties to the 30 appraisal any potential conflict of interest. 31 (2) An appraiser shall not engage in any act or practice 32 that is a conflict of interest during the appraisal. 33 (3) If a conflict of interest arises after the start of the 34 appraisal process, an appraiser shall disclose the conflict of 35 -61- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 61/ 106 S.F. 619 interest to the parties and shall withdraw from the appraisal 1 process no more than five business days after the conflict of 2 interest arose. 3 b. A conflict of interest shall include but is not limited 4 to all of the following: 5 (1) An appraiser is a party to a lawsuit against any party 6 to an appraisal. 7 (2) An appraiser is a party to, or a member or employee 8 of a law firm that represents a party to, a current lawsuit 9 involving an insurer that is a party to the appraisal. 10 (3) An appraiser has personally investigated, prosecuted, 11 or advocated in connection with the appraisal. 12 (4) An appraiser has acted as counsel to any party to 13 an appraisal within the two years immediately preceding the 14 appraisal. 15 (5) An appraiser has a personal financial interest in the 16 outcome of the appraisal or any other significant interest 17 that could be substantially affected by the outcome of the 18 appraisal. 19 (6) A member of an appraiserâs immediate family is any of 20 the following: 21 (a) A party to the appraisal, or an officer, director, or 22 trustee of a party. 23 (b) A current employee of an appraiser or an adjuster to the 24 appraisal. 25 (c) A business entity licensed as an adjuster that adjusted 26 the loss at issue in the appraisal. 27 (d) Known to have an interest that could be substantially 28 affected by the outcome of the appraisal. 29 (e) An immediate family member that has a legally sufficient 30 reason that requires the appraiser to withdraw from the 31 appraisal. 32 3. An appraiser shall postpone an appraisal for a reasonable 33 amount of time if any party demonstrates reasonable cause for 34 a postponement. The appraiser shall notify all parties if 35 -62- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 62/ 106 S.F. 619 the appraisal process is postponed. An appraiserâs failure 1 to timely notify all parties may result in a penalty under 2 sections 522F.20 and 522F.21. 3 4. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall 4 consider all information provided by the parties and any 5 other reasonably available evidence that is material to the 6 appraisal. 7 5. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall 8 carefully decide all issues submitted for determination of the 9 amount of loss and actual cash value. 10 6. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall provide 11 all parties a fair and reasonable itemized written appraisal 12 detailing the amount of loss and actual cash value. 13 7. In the course of an appraisal, an appraiser shall ensure 14 the appraiserâs party is reasonably informed of all updates 15 throughout the appraisal process. 16 8. An appraiser shall not permit outside influence to affect 17 an appraisal. 18 9. An appraiser shall not allow a person other than the 19 umpire for the appraisal to determine differences between the 20 actual cash value and the amount of loss of each item on the 21 appraisal. 22 10. a. An appraiser shall not communicate directly or 23 indirectly with any of the following: 24 (1) An opposing party or representative of the opposing 25 party other than the opposing partyâs appraiser. 26 (2) The umpire, unless reasonable notice and opportunity 27 to participate in the communication is provided to an opposing 28 appraiser. 29 b. Notwithstanding paragraph âaâ , an appraiser may 30 communicate with an opposing party or an umpire in order to do 31 any of the following: 32 (1) Identify the partyâs counsel or experts. 33 (2) Discuss logistical matters, including the time and 34 place of a meeting or to make arrangements for the conduct 35 -63- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 63/ 106 S.F. 619 of the appraisal. The appraiser initiating contact with the 1 umpire shall promptly inform an opposing appraiser. 2 (3) If an opposing appraiser fails to participate in a 3 meeting or conference call after receiving reasonable notice 4 and opportunity to participate, or if all parties agree 5 in writing in advance of a meeting or conference call, an 6 appraiser may discuss a claim with the umpire. 7 11. An appraiser shall not act as, or have ever acted as, an 8 adjuster or umpire on the same claim. 9 12. An appraiser shall not withdraw or abandon an appraisal 10 unless compelled by unforeseen circumstances that would render 11 it impossible or impracticable for the appraiser to continue. 12 13. During the appraisal process, an appraiser may hire 13 an outside expert to provide subject matter expertise as 14 necessary. 15 Sec. 63. NEW SECTION . 522F.8 Umpire license ââ eligibility. 16 1. NEW SECTION . 522F.13 Umpires ââ standards of 16 conduct. 17 1. An umpire shall act with due diligence, including but 18 not limited to demonstrating accuracy, fairness, and timeliness 19 throughout an appraisal process. 20 2. a. (1) No later than three business days after being 21 hired by the parties to an appraisal and before beginning work 22 as an umpire to the appraisal, an umpire shall disclose to all 23 parties to the appraisal any potential conflict of interest. 24 If a conflict of interest exists, the umpire shall withdraw 25 from the appraisal. 26 (2) An umpire shall not engage in any act or practice that 27 is a conflict of interest during the appraisal. 28 (3) If a conflict of interest arises after the start of an 29 appraisal process, an umpire shall disclose the conflict of 30 interest to the parties and shall withdraw from the appraisal 31 process. 32 b. A conflict of interest shall include but is not limited 33 to the following: 34 (1) An umpire is a party to a lawsuit against any party to 35 -68- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 68/ 106 S.F. 619 an appraisal. 1 (2) An umpire is a party to, or a member or employee of 2 a law firm that represents a party to, a current lawsuit 3 involving an insurer that is party to the appraisal. 4 (3) An umpire has a personal open claim involving an insurer 5 that is a party to the appraisal. 6 (4) An umpire has a personal bias or prejudice against a 7 party. 8 (5) An umpire has personally investigated, prosecuted, or 9 advocated in connection with the appraisal. 10 (6) An umpire has acted as counsel to any party to an 11 appraisal within the two years immediately preceding the 12 appraisal. 13 (7) An umpire has a personal financial interest in the 14 outcome of the appraisal or any other significant interest 15 that could be substantially affected by the outcome of the 16 appraisal. 17 (8) A member of an umpireâs immediate family is any of the 18 following: 19 (a) A party to the appraisal, or an officer, director, or 20 trustee of a party. 21 (b) A current employee of an appraiser or an adjuster to the 22 appraisal. 23 (c) A business entity licensed as an adjuster that adjusted 24 the loss at issue in the appraisal. 25 (d) Known to have an interest that could be substantially 26 affected by the outcome of the appraisal. 27 (e) An immediate family member that has a legally sufficient 28 reason that requires the umpire to withdraw from the appraisal. 29 3. Prior to beginning work as an umpire, an umpire shall 30 enter into a written contract with all parties to the appraisal 31 that requires the parties and the umpire to comply with this 32 section, and provides that each party shall pay costs as 33 required under section 522F.11. 34 4. An umpire shall not begin work on a claim until the 35 -69- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 69/ 106 S.F. 619 umpire receives each appraiserâs differences in actual cash 1 value and amount of loss of each item of the claim, and written 2 approval from the parties for the umpire to begin work. 3 5. No later than three business days after receiving notice 4 of selection for an appraisal, an umpire shall send notice 5 to the parties and the appraisers that includes all of the 6 following: 7 a. A statement informing each party if the umpire is insured 8 by an insurer. 9 b. A statement informing each party of the partyâs 10 respective right to object to the umpire under section 522F.12. 11 6. An umpire shall address only issues in an appraisal that 12 the appraisers disagree on. 13 7. An umpire shall review all information submitted by the 14 appraisers and parties related to the dispute, including but 15 not limited to the itemized appraisals or estimates, supporting 16 documents, photographs, and diagrams. The umpire shall review 17 the differences between what each appraiser submitted and seek 18 agreement by the appraisers regarding the disputed issues. 19 8. An umpire shall allow each appraiser to a claim a fair 20 opportunity to present evidence and arguments regarding the 21 appraisal. 22 9. An umpire shall ask questions, or request documents or 23 other evidence, as the umpire deems necessary in the course of 24 an appraisal. 25 10. An umpire may accept either appraiserâs scope, 26 quantity, value, or cost regarding an item in dispute, or 27 develop an independent decision on each item in dispute. 28 11. An umpire shall decide all matters in an appraisal 29 fairly, and shall exercise independent judgment and integrity. 30 12. An umpire shall prepare and distribute a written 31 itemized award pursuant to section 522F.16. 32 13. An umpire shall not visit the claimantâs damaged 33 property without consent from all appraisers. 34 14. An umpire shall not withdraw or abandon an appraisal 35 -70- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 70/ 106 S.F. 619 unless compelled by unforeseen circumstances that would render 1 it impossible or impracticable for the umpire to continue on a 2 claim. 3 15. An umpire shall not attend or participate in settlement 4 discussions unless requested to do so by all parties. 5 16. An umpire shall not permit outside influences to affect 6 an appraisal. 7 17. An umpire shall not delegate the umpireâs duty to decide 8 a claim to any other person. 9 18. Unless reasonable notice and opportunity to participate 10 in a communication is provided to an opposing party and the 11 opposing partyâs appraiser, an umpire shall not communicate, 12 directly or indirectly, with any party or appraiser regarding a 13 pending appraisal. 14 19. Unless reasonable notice and opportunity to participate 15 in a communication is provided to all parties, an umpire shall 16 not communicate, directly or indirectly, with any party, a 17 representative of any party, or any other person with a direct 18 or indirect interest in the claim, regarding an issue of fact 19 or law in the appraisal. 20 20. An umpire shall not act as, or have ever acted as, an 21 adjuster or appraiser on the same claim. 22 Sec. 69. NEW SECTION . 522F.14 Appraisal process. 23 1. This section provides for the appraisal process if all 24 of the following apply: 25 a. The claimantâs insurance policy is delivered, issued for 26 delivery, or renewed in this state. 27 b. The property that is the subject of the claimantâs 28 claim is located in this state, or the dispute is subject to 29 jurisdiction in this state. 30 c. A claimant gave proper notice to the claimantâs insurer 31 of a loss claim, and the claimant and insurer dispute the 32 actual cash value of the scope of loss, or the amount of loss 33 the insurer will pay, for the claimantâs claim under the 34 claimantâs policy. The claimant and the insurer must both 35 -71- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 71/ 106 S.F. 619 provide the other party with a scope of loss of a covered 1 peril, including a list stating separately the actual cash 2 value and the amount of claimed loss for each item. 3 d. The claimant or insurer demands in writing an appraisal. 4 2. Within twenty calendar days following either the 5 claimantâs or insurerâs receipt of the other partyâs written 6 demand for an appraisal, the claimant and the insurer 7 shall each select an appraiser from the appraiser list. 8 Upon selection, the appraiser shall attest in writing to 9 the selecting party that the appraiser is competent and 10 disinterested with regards to the appraisal in question. 11 3. a. Within fifteen calendar days of the selection of 12 appraisers pursuant to subsection 2, both appraisers shall 13 agree on an umpire from the umpire list. 14 b. A party or an appraiser may object to the agreed-upon 15 umpire for good cause pursuant to section 522F.12 no later 16 than five business days after the umpire has been selected. A 17 replacement umpire from the umpire list shall then be agreed 18 upon by both appraisers. 19 c. If both appraisers fail to agree on an umpire, either the 20 claimant or insurer shall immediately provide written notice 21 to the division, in the form and manner prescribed by the 22 division, and the division shall randomly select an umpire from 23 the umpire list and notify the parties. 24 d. If either appraiser requests that an umpire be selected 25 by a judge in the state in which the property that is the 26 subject of the claim is located, a judge shall give deference 27 to the randomly selected umpire from the umpire list by the 28 division unless either the claimant or the insurer provides 29 good cause for the judge to make an alternative selection from 30 the umpire list. 31 4. Within forty-five calendar days from the date the 32 umpire is selected, both appraisers shall appraise the loss, 33 stating separately the actual cash value and the amount of 34 loss for each item. Each appraiser shall submit separately 35 -72- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 72/ 106 S.F. 619 the appraiserâs actual cash value and amount of loss of each 1 item, along with any supporting information, to the umpire. 2 Each appraiser shall also submit written authorization for the 3 umpire to commence the umpireâs work. 4 5. No later than forty-five calendar days after receipt of 5 the actual cash value and amount of loss under subsection 4, 6 the umpire shall prepare and provide to the parties and each 7 appraiser a written itemized award showing the actual cash 8 value and amount of loss. The written itemized award shall 9 include but is not limited to all of the following: 10 a. Contact information for each appraiser and the umpire. 11 b. The insuredâs policy number and the insuredâs claim 12 number. 13 c. The date of the insuredâs loss. 14 d. The type of covered peril that caused the loss. 15 e. The date the umpire commenced work. 16 f. The legal name of the insurer. 17 g. The physical address of the property on which the insured 18 made a claim. 19 h. The date of the umpireâs written itemized award. 20 i. (1) A description and itemization of the final written 21 itemized award by coverage type, including but not limited to: 22 (a) Coverage A ââ dwelling. 23 (b) Coverage B ââ other structures. 24 (c) Coverage C ââ personal property. 25 (2) The description and itemization by coverage type shall 26 include contested items that have been resolved, sublimits, 27 and other disputed items. Items, including but not limited 28 to items with sublimits, shall be separately noted to avoid 29 ambiguity in the final written itemized award. 30 j. The signature of the umpire and at least one appraiser. 31 6. Prior to the umpire issuing the written itemized award, 32 the parties may agree to conclude the appraisal process when 33 the parties reach a final settlement. 34 Sec. 70. NEW SECTION . 522F.19 Hearings ââ service of 18 process, attendance of witnesses, and production of documents. 19 1. Whenever the commissioner believes that a person has 20 been engaged, or is engaging, in a violation of this chapter 21 or a rule adopted or an order issued under this chapter, and 22 that a proceeding by the commissioner would be in the public 23 interest, the commissioner shall issue and serve upon the 24 person a statement of the charges and a notice of a hearing on 25 the charges to be held at the time and place set in the notice, 26 which shall not be less than ten business days after the date 27 of service of such notice. 28 2. At the time and place of such hearing, the person shall 29 have an opportunity to be heard and to show cause why an order 30 should not be made by the commissioner requiring the person to 31 cease and desist from the violation of the chapter, rule, or 32 order. Upon a showing of good cause, the commissioner shall 33 permit any person, by counsel or in person, to intervene, 34 appear, and be heard at such hearing. 35 -75- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 75/ 106 S.F. 619 3. A hearing under this section shall not be required to 1 observe formal rules of pleading or evidence. 2 4. The commissioner, at a hearing under this section, may 3 administer oaths, examine and cross-examine witnesses, receive 4 oral and documentary evidence, and may subpoena witnesses, 5 compel their attendance, and require the production of books, 6 papers, records, correspondence, or other documents which the 7 commissioner deems relevant. The commissioner may, and upon 8 the request of any party shall, cause to be made a stenographic 9 record of the evidence and proceedings of a hearing under this 10 section. If no stenographic record is made and if a judicial 11 review is sought, the commissioner shall prepare a statement 12 of the evidence and proceeding for use on review. If a person 13 refuses to comply with a subpoena issued under this section, 14 or to testify to a matter for which the person may lawfully be 15 interrogated, the district court of Polk county or the district 16 court of the county where the person resides, on application of 17 the commissioner, may issue an order requiring such person to 18 comply with such subpoena or to testify. Failure of a person 19 to obey such order of the court may be punished by the court as 20 contempt. 21 5. NEW SECTION . 522F.21 Civil and criminal penalties. 19 1. a. Upon a determination by the commissioner, after 20 a hearing conducted pursuant to chapter 17A, that a person 21 violated this chapter, the commissioner shall reduce the 22 findings of the hearing to writing and deliver a copy of the 23 findings to the person. 24 b. Upon a determination by the commissioner that a person 25 has engaged, is engaging, or is about to engage in any act or 26 practice constituting a violation of this chapter or a rule 27 adopted or order issued under this chapter, the commissioner 28 may take the following actions: 29 (1) Issue an order requiring the person to cease and desist 30 from engaging in the conduct resulting in the violation. 31 (2) Assess a civil penalty against the person of not more 32 than one thousand dollars for each violation not to exceed an 33 aggregate of ten thousand dollars. 34 (3) If the person knew or reasonably should have known the 35 -80- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 80/ 106 S.F. 619 person was in violation of this chapter, assess a civil penalty 1 of not more than five thousand dollars for each violation 2 of this chapter not to exceed an aggregate penalty of fifty 3 thousand dollars in any one six-month period. 4 (4) (a) Issue a summary order, including a brief statement 5 of findings of fact, conclusions of law, and policy reasons for 6 the decision, and directing the person to cease and desist from 7 engaging in the act or practice or to take affirmative action 8 as is necessary in the judgment of the commissioner to comply 9 with the requirements of this chapter. 10 (b) A person may contest a summary order by filing, 11 within thirty calendar days from the date of the issuance of 12 the summary order, a written request for a contested case 13 proceeding and hearing as provided in chapter 17A and in 14 accordance with rules adopted by the commissioner. Section 15 17A.18A shall be inapplicable to a summary order issued under 16 this subsection. If a hearing is not requested within thirty 17 calendar days from the date of issuance of the summary order, 18 the summary order shall become final by operation of law. A 19 summary order shall remain effective from the date of issuance 20 until the date the order becomes final by operation of law, 21 or is modified or overturned by a presiding officer or court 22 following a request for hearing. 23 (c) A person violating a summary order issued under this 24 subsection shall be deemed in contempt of the summary order. 25 The commissioner may petition the district court to enforce the 26 order as certified by the commissioner. The district court 27 shall find the person in contempt of the order if the court 28 finds, after conducting a hearing, that the person is not 29 in compliance with the order. The court may assess a civil 30 penalty against the person and may issue further orders as the 31 court deems appropriate. 32 c. In addition to any other penalty under this section, 33 if the commissioner finds that a violation of this chapter 34 was directed, encouraged, condoned, ignored, or ratified by 35 -81- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 81/ 106 S.F. 619 the employer of the appraiser or umpire, the commissioner 1 shall assess a penalty to the employer. Penalties under this 2 paragraph may be retained by the commissioner under the fund 3 described in section 505.7, subsection 9. 4 2. a. A person acting as an appraiser or an umpire without 5 proper licensure, or an appraiser or an umpire who willfully 6 violates any provision of this chapter or an order issued 7 under this chapter, is guilty of a class âDâ felony. If the 8 violation results in a loss of more than ten thousand dollars, 9 the appraiser or an umpire is guilty of a class âCâ felony. 10 b. The commissioner may refer such evidence as is available 11 concerning a violation of this chapter, or of any rule adopted 12 or order issued under this chapter, or of the failure of a 13 person to comply with the licensing requirements of this 14 chapter, to the attorney general or the proper district 15 attorney who may institute the appropriate criminal proceedings 16 under this chapter. 17 c. This chapter shall not limit the power of the state to 18 punish any person for any conduct that constitutes a crime 19 under any other statute. 20 Sec. 77.
