EFFECTIVE DATE. This division of this Act, being 33 deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon enactment. 34 EXPLANATION 35 -90- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 90/ 106 S.F. 619 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with 1 the explanationâs substance by the members of the general assembly. 2 This bill relates to the natural hazard mitigation financing 3 program, the disaster recovery housing assistance program, the 4 disaster recovery new housing program, post-loss assignments 5 of benefits, and the licensing and regulation of adjusters, 6 appraisers and umpires. 7 DIVISION I ââ NATURAL HAZARD MITIGATION FINANCING PROGRAM. 8 The bill creates the natural hazard mitigation financing 9 program (program) for the purpose of making loans available 10 to eligible entities to finance all or part of the costs of a 11 project. âEligible entityâ and âprojectâ are defined in the 12 bill. The program shall be a joint and cooperative undertaking 13 of the department of homeland security and emergency management 14 (HSEMD) and the Iowa finance authority (IFA). 15 The bill creates a natural hazard mitigation revolving loan 16 fund (fund) under the control of HSEMD, in consultation with 17 IFA, consisting of moneys and program funding as detailed in 18 the bill. 19 HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, may establish and maintain 20 funds or accounts necessary to carry out the purposes of the 21 bill. Any moneys appropriated to HSEMD and IFA for purposes 22 of paying the costs and expenses associated with the program 23 shall be administered as determined by IFA. The funds or 24 accounts are separate dedicated funds and accounts under the 25 administration and control of IFA, and shall not be considered 26 part of the general fund of the state, are not subject to 27 appropriation for any other purpose by the general assembly, 28 and in determining a general fund balance shall not be included 29 in the general fund of the state, but shall remain in the funds 30 and accounts maintained by HSEMD or IFA. IFA may provide for 31 the issuance of bonds or notes as detailed in the bill. 32 The duties of the director of HSEMD (director) are detailed 33 in the bill. 34 For the fiscal year beginning July 1, 2025, and each fiscal 35 -91- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 91/ 106 S.F. 619 year thereafter, HSEMD may prepare and deliver intended use 1 plans to, and enter into capitalization grant agreements with, 2 the administrator of the United States federal emergency 3 management agency and may accept capitalization grants for the 4 fund. HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, shall establish fiscal 5 controls and accounting procedures for the fund. 6 HSEMD and IFA shall review each loan application to 7 determine if the applicant is an eligible entity and qualifies 8 for a loan. IFA, in cooperation with HSEMD, shall determine 9 the interest rate and repayment terms for each loan under the 10 program and shall enter into a loan agreement with each loan 11 recipient. IFA may charge loan recipients fees and assess 12 costs as necessary. 13 Moneys in the fund shall be used for the primary purpose of 14 making loans to eligible entities to finance eligible costs of 15 projects in accordance with the intended use plans. The loan 16 recipients and the purpose and amount of the loans shall be 17 determined by the director. 18 HSEMD, in consultation with IFA, shall adopt rules pursuant 19 to Code chapter 17A to administer the division of the bill. 20 The bill makes a conforming change to Code section 422.7. 21 DIVISION II ââ DISASTER RECOVERY HOUSING ASSISTANCE PROGRAM. 22 The bill requires a state of disaster emergency proclamation 23 by the governor that authorizes disaster recovery housing 24 assistance to specify if disaster recovery housing assistance 25 is available to homeowners, renters, or both homeowners and 26 renters. 27 The bill defines âfinancial assistanceâ as assistance 28 provided only from the funds, rights, and assets legally 29 available to IFA and includes but is not limited to assistance 30 in the form of grants, loans, and forgivable loans. 31 Under the bill, IFA shall not use more than 5 percent of the 32 moneys deposited into the disaster recovery housing assistance 33 fund for administrative and program costs. 34 Under current law, to be considered for financial assistance 35 -92- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 92/ 106 S.F. 619 under the disaster recovery housing assistance program, 1 a homeowner or renter must register for the disaster case 2 advocacy program. Under the bill, a homeowner or renter is not 3 required to register for the advocacy program to be considered 4 for financial assistance under the disaster recovery housing 5 assistance program. 6 The bill makes conforming changes to Code section 16.57B. 7 DIVISION III ââ DISASTER RECOVERY NEW HOUSING PROGRAM. The 8 bill defines âqualifying state disaster recovery new housing 9 grantâ (grant) as an award of a state disaster recovery new 10 housing grant that was applied for between August 20, 2024, 11 and December 31, 2024, and approved and issued by the economic 12 development authority. A grant shall not be included in the 13 computation of net income for federal income tax purposes. 14 Code section 422.7, subsection 45, and Code section 422.35, 15 subsection 14, are repealed January 1, 2028. 16 The division takes effect upon enactment and applies 17 retroactively to tax years beginning on or after January 1, 18 2024. 19 DIVISION IV ââ POST-LOSS ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS ââ 20 RESIDENTIAL CONTRACTOR. Under the bill, a violation of Code 21 section 515.137 is an unfair method of competition and unfair 22 or deceptive act or practice in the business of insurance. 23 The bill defines âpost-loss assignmentâ (assignment). The 24 assignment must only assign the insurance proceeds a named 25 insured is entitled to receive from the named insuredâs insurer 26 for the repair, replacement construction, or reconstruction of 27 the named insuredâs property. 28 A residential contractor (contractor) shall not engage 29 in conduct prohibited by the bill under an assignment by a 30 named insured to the contractor under a property and casualty 31 insurance policy. 32 An assignment must include an itemized description 33 containing the information detailed in the bill. 34 An assignment shall not impair the interest of a mortgagee, 35 -93- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 93/ 106 S.F. 619 and all mortgagees shall be named as a co-payee for the payment 1 of benefits. An assignment shall only authorize a contractor 2 to be named as a co-payee, along with the named insured and all 3 mortgagees, for the payment of benefits. An assignment shall 4 not prevent or inhibit an insurer from communicating with the 5 named insured or a mortgagee. 6 An electronic copy of a fully executed assignment shall 7 be provided to a named insured and all mortgagees of the 8 damaged residential real estate within five business days after 9 execution. A contractor named in an assignment must cooperate 10 with the insurer in a claim investigation. 11 A named insured shall have the right to cancel an assignment 12 without penalty or fee under the circumstances detailed in the 13 bill. 14 Any written contract, repair estimate, or work order 15 prepared by a contractor to provide goods or services pursuant 16 to an assignment shall include notice as provided in the bill 17 which shall be signed by the named insured and sent to the 18 named insuredâs insurer prior to payment. 19 For at least 72 hours following a catastrophic disaster, a 20 residential contractor shall not enter into a contract with 21 an insured that includes an assignment. If the severity of 22 the catastrophic disaster has placed people under duress, as 23 determined by the commissioner, the commissioner shall dispatch 24 the consumer advocate and personnel to provide consumer 25 guidance. The commissioner may extend the 72-hour period by an 26 additional 72 hours after public hearing. 27 An assignment entered into with a contractor shall be void if 28 the contractor violates the bill. 29 DIVISION V ââ PUBLIC, INDEPENDENT, AND STAFF ADJUSTERS. The 30 bill makes conforming changes to Code sections 522B.5A and 31 522C.1. 32 Under current law, the commissioner of insurance 33 (commissioner) shall adopt rules as necessary to administer and 34 enforce Code chapter 522C. Under the bill, the commissioner 35 -94- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 94/ 106 S.F. 619 may adopt such rules. 1 Under the bill, a person shall not act as, or represent that 2 the person is, a public adjuster or an independent adjuster 3 unless the person is licensed. A license as an adjuster is 4 not required for a staff adjuster, an attorney when acting 5 within their professional capacity as an attorney, or a person 6 employed only for the purpose of obtaining facts surrounding a 7 loss or to furnish technical assistance to a licensed adjuster. 8 A person applying for an adjuster license shall complete an 9 application as described in the bill. The commissioner may 10 require a criminal history check for the applicant. 11 Prior to approving an application for a resident adjuster 12 license, a nonresident adjuster license, or a business entityâs 13 or nonresident business entityâs application for a license for 14 a resident public adjuster or resident independent adjuster, 15 the commissioner shall find that the applicant meets the 16 requirements detailed in the bill. 17 If the commissioner does not renew a license or denies 18 an application for a license, the commissioner shall notify 19 the applicant or licensee and advise of the reason for the 20 nonrenewal or denial. Within 30 calendar days of the date of 21 the notice, the licensee or applicant may request a hearing on 22 the nonrenewal or denial. 23 Application fees for a license as an adjuster are detailed 24 in the bill. The fee for an examination may be set by a 25 third-party testing service and must be approved by the 26 division of insurance (division). 27 Prior to issuance of a license, an applicant shall secure 28 evidence of financial responsibility (responsibility) through 29 a surety bond (bond) as prescribed by the commissioner. The 30 bond shall be executed and issued by an insurer authorized 31 to issue bonds, and must meet the requirements of the 32 bill. The division may request that an adjuster provide 33 evidence of responsibility at any time. An adjuster shall 34 immediately notify the division if the adjusterâs evidence 35 -95- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 95/ 106 S.F. 619 of responsibility terminates or becomes impaired, and the 1 adjusterâs license shall become inactive. 2 An individual applying for a license shall pass a written 3 examination, unless exempt, as described in the bill. An 4 individual who concurrently applies for an adjuster license and 5 an appraiser license may choose to take a joint examination as 6 detailed in the bill. An individual who successfully passes a 7 joint examination and meets the licensure requirements shall be 8 licensed as both an adjuster and an appraiser. 9 A public adjuster shall not provide services to an insured 10 until a written contract with the insured has been executed. 11 The contract must meet all of the requirements detailed in the 12 bill. No provisions in the contract shall be redacted in a 13 copy of the contract submitted to the commissioner. 14 If the insurer, no later than five calendar days after the 15 date on which the insuredâs loss is reported, either pays 16 or commits in writing to pay the policy limits, the public 17 adjuster shall inform the insured that the total amount of 18 loss claimed by the insured may not be paid by the insured, 19 and the adjuster is only entitled to reasonable compensation 20 from the insured. Prior to execution of a contract, the public 21 adjuster shall review the terms of the contract with the 22 insured and provide a separate disclosure document that meets 23 the requirements detailed in the bill. 24 An original copy of a completed contract shall be provided 25 to the public adjuster and kept by the insured. A contract 26 may be executed electronically if done so in compliance with 27 Code chapter 554D. Within 72 hours of entering a contract with 28 an insured, the public adjuster shall provide the insuredâs 29 insurer a notification letter. An appraiser or an 1 umpire who surrendered a license and stated an intent to exit 2 the appraiser business may file a request to reactivate the 3 license within 90 calendar days of the date the license was 4 placed on inactive status. 5 Each party to an appraisal shall be responsible for the 6 partyâs own appraiserâs fees and expenses, an equal share of 7 all reasonable and necessary fees and expenses incurred by an 8 umpire, and an equal share of all reasonable and necessary 9 costs incurred in the course of conducting the appraisal. The 25 claimant and the insurer must both provide the other party with 26 a list stating separately the actual cash value and the amount 27 of claimed loss for each item at issue. Within 20 calendar 28 days of receipt of a written demand for an appraisal, the 29 claimant and the insurer shall each select an appraiser from 30 the appraiser list. Upon selection, the appraiser shall attest 31 that the appraiser is competent and disinterested with regards 32 to the appraisal. 33 Within 15 calendar days of the selection of appraisers, both 34 appraisers shall agree on an umpire from the umpire list. A 35 -101- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 101/ 106 S.F. 619 party or an appraiser may object to the umpire for good cause 1 no later than five business days after the umpire has been 2 selected. If both appraisers fail to 4 agree on an umpire, the division shall randomly select an 5 umpire from the umpire list and notify the parties. Under current law, moneys in the 26 Iowa economic emergency fund may only be used pursuant to 27 an appropriation by the general assembly, including for 28 purposes of reducing or preventing an overdraft on or deficit 29 in the general fund of the state. Each fiscal year, the 30 bill appropriates up to 10 percent of the maximum balance 31 of the Iowa economic emergency fund, as calculated for the 32 immediately preceding fiscal year, to the department of 33 management (DOM) for disaster response, disaster recovery 34 activities, or disaster aid to citizens, at the direction of 35 -105- LSB 1094SZ (3) 91 nls/ko 105/ 106 S.F. 619 the governor, with the approval of the executive council, 1 following a proclamation of disaster emergency. The bill 2 allows DOM, subject to approval of the governor, to provide 3 for an interdepartmental transfer of the moneys to another 4 state entity for the purposes specified, notwithstanding the 5 limitations and requirements of Code section 8.39, including 6 notification of the general assembly. 7 DIVISION VIII ââ IOWA ECONOMIC EMERGENCY FUND ââ 8 APPROPRIATIONS.
